Proof from Quran: Misguidance from Pharaoh and Satan
Author presents four Quranic proofs attributing misguidance to created beings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how four Quranic verses attribute misguidance to Pharaoh, Satan, and the people themselves, refuting the idea that Allah creates disbelief.

Core Idea
Misguidance is from human and satanic agents, not from Allah.

The author continues with more Quranic proofs that misguidance and disbelief originate from created beings, not from Allah. These verses explicitly state that Pharaoh led his people astray, Satan desires to mislead, and the people themselves are the source of their envy and hypocrisy. This lesson covers four such verses.

Guided Path
1
Read the next four verses
Read verses f, g, h, and t with their commentaries. Notice the attribution of misguidance to Pharaoh and Satan.
2
Focus on verse f
Verse f says Pharaoh led his people astray. The author comments: if it were from Allah, it would not be from Pharaoh.
This is a clear disassociation of Allah from misguidance.
3
Understand verse t
Verse t narrates the people of the Fire admitting they tempted themselves. The author says this is explicit that Allah has no hand in disbelief.
This is a strong proof.
4
Reflect on the restriction in verse h
Verse h says 'disbelievers, out of envy from themselves'. The author emphasizes 'from themselves'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ب - قلتم : أني هذا ؟ قل : هو من عند أنفسكم (١) ج - ( فكلا أخذنا بذنبه (٢) ) فلو كان حصول الذنب بخلق الله ، لكان مؤاخذاً لا بذنب نفسه ، بل بالذنب الذي فعله فيه غيره . د - ( وما ظلمناهم ولكن كانوا هم الظالمين (٣) ) وهذا تصريح بأن ذلك ليس من الله بل منهم . هـ - ( إنما يريد الله أن يصيبهم ببعض ذنوبهم (٤)) وكيف يصيبهم بذنوبهم ، ولا ذنب لهم في تلك الأفعال ، التي هي الكفر والمعصية كما لا ذنب لهم في وجود السماء والأرض ؟ و - ( وأضل فرعون قومه وما هدى (٥) ) وهذا تصريح بأن الضلال من فرعون ولو كان من عند الله ما كان من فرعون . ز - ويريد الشيطان أن يضلهم ضلالاً بعيداً (٦) ) ح - ( كفاراً حسداً من عند أنفسهم (٧) ) وهذا تصريح بأن ذلك الفعل من عند أنفسهم . ط - قال تعالى حكاية عن أهل النار ينادونهم : ألم نكن معكم ؟ قالوا : بلى ولكنكم فتنتم أنفسكم وتربصتم وارتبتم وغرتكم الأماني (٨) ) وهذا نص صريح في أنه لا صنع الله في الكفر . ى - إنما النجوى من الشيطان ليحزن الذين آمنوا (٩) ) وكلمة إنما للحصر ي - الشيطان سول لهم ، وأملى لهم (١٠) يب - ما يفعل الله بعذابكم إن شكرتم وآمنتم (١١) ) ؟ وهذا يفسد قول من يقول : إنه خلق الكفر في الدنيا ثم يعذبه عليه في الآخرة ، وإنه تعالى ما خلقه إلا لهذا العذاب . وأمثال هذه الآيات كثيرة فنكتف بهذا القدر
B. You said: 'Whence is this?' Say: 'It is from yourselves' (1). C. 'And each We seized for his sin' (2). If sin came about by Allah’s creation, He would be taking one to task not for his own sin, but for the sin that another did in him. D. 'And We did not wrong them, but they were the wrongdoers' (3). This is an explicit statement that that is not from Allah, but from them. E. 'Allah only desires to afflict them with some of their sins' (4). How can He afflict them with their sins when they have no sin in those acts which are disbelief and disobedience, just as they have no sin in the existence of the heavens and the earth? F. 'And Pharaoh led his people astray and did not guide [them]' (5). This is an explicit statement that misguidance is from Pharaoh; had it been from Allah, it would not be from Pharaoh. G. 'And Satan desires to lead them far astray' (6). H. 'Disbelievers, out of envy from themselves' (7). This is an explicit statement that that act is from themselves. T. Allah Almighty said, narrating about the people of the Fire calling out to them: 'Were we not with you?' They said: 'Yes, but you tempted yourselves, and waited, and doubted, and delusions deceived you' (8). This is an explicit text that Allah has no hand in disbelief. Y. 'Private conversation is only from Satan, to grieve those who believe' (9). The word 'innama' indicates restriction. K. 'Satan tempted them and gave them false hope' (10). L. 'What would Allah do with your punishment if you are grateful and believe?' (11). This invalidates the saying of whoever says: He created disbelief in the world, then punishes for it in the Hereafter, and that the Exalted only created it for this punishment. And similar verses are many; we suffice with this amount.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is a series of proofs from the Quran refuting the Jabriyya claim that sins are created by Allah and then He punishes people for them. The author proceeds alphabetically, citing each verse and immediately explaining how it disproves the Jabriyya position. The first verse (Al-Imran 3:165) commands the Prophet to say that what befell them is from themselves. The second (Al-Ankabut 29:40) states that each was seized for his own sin, implying responsibility. The author argues: if sin were created by Allah, He would be punishing for another's act. Next (Az-Zukhruf 43:76) explicitly says they wronged themselves, not Allah. Then (Al-Ma'idah 5:50) says Allah only afflicts them with some of their sins, raising the question: how can He afflict them for sins they did not commit (if He created their disbelief)? Next (Ta-Ha 20:79) says Pharaoh led his people astray, so misguidance is attributed to Pharaoh. Then (An-Nisa 4:60) mentions Satan's desire to lead astray. Then (Al-Baqarah 2:109) says the disbelief was from envy from themselves. Then (Al-Hadid 57:14) has the people of the Fire admitting they tempted themselves. Then (Al-Mujadilah 58:10) uses 'innama' to restrict evil conversation to Satan. Then (Muhammad 47:25) says Satan tempted them. Finally (An-Nisa 4:147) asks what Allah would gain from punishing them if they are grateful and believe, demonstrating that punishment is contingent on their own actions, not on a predetermined creation of disbelief. The author concludes that many such verses exist and he has sufficed with this amount.

Key Terms
الضلال
الإضلال
الكفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah is the one who leads people astray and creates disbelief in them.
Correction: The Quran attributes misguidance to Pharaoh and Satan, and disbelief to the people themselves.

Checkpoint
According to verse f (Ta-Ha 20:79), who led Pharaoh's people astray?
A) Allah
B) Pharaoh
C) Satan
D) The people themselves

Key Takeaway
The Quran explicitly attributes misguidance to created beings, not to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself in sin or spiritual doubt, do you ever blame Allah's decree? How might the verses about Pharaoh and the people of the Fire change your view of your personal responsibility? What will you do today to stop attributing your failures to fate and start owning them?
?
The people of the Fire admitted to four things: self-temptation, waiting (procrastination), doubt, and being deceived by delusions. Which of these do you see most in your own life right now? Will you take one specific, actionable step this week to combat that particular enemy within you?
?
If Allah has no hand in disbelief, as this passage explicitly states, then what does that mean for the excuses you make for your disobedience? How will you begin to truly believe that your choices are yours alone—and what are you going to do about that today?

Proof from Quran: No Divine Hand in Disbelief
Author presents final verses and concludes that Allah does not create disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the final set of Quranic verses and the author's conclusion refute the claim that Allah creates disbelief and then punishes for it.

Core Idea
Evil conversations are from Satan, and punishment depends on human thankfulness, not on created disbelief.

The author concludes his series of proofs with three more verses and a final remark. These verses emphasize that evil whispers are from Satan, not Allah, and that punishment is contingent on human gratitude and faith. The author then states that these verses invalidate the Jabriyya position that Allah creates disbelief for the purpose of punishment.

Guided Path
1
Read the final verses
Read verses y, k, and l with their commentaries. Note the restrictive language in verse y.
2
Understand the restriction in verse y
Verse y uses 'innama' (only) to restrict evil conversation to Satan. This implies Allah does not originate it.
'Innama' is a tool of restriction.
3
Analyze verse l
Verse l asks what Allah would gain from punishing if they are grateful. This shows punishment is not for created disbelief but for ungratefulness.
4
Read the author's conclusion
The author says this invalidates the claim that Allah created disbelief to punish. Reflect on why.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you fall into sin, do you ever catch yourself thinking that Allah created that sin in you? How does this lesson challenge that thought, and what will you do the next time that thought arises?
?
If punishment truly depends on your gratitude and belief, not on Allah's decree of disbelief, then what excuse do you have for neglecting thankfulness? Will you start a daily habit of naming three things you are grateful to Allah for?
?
This lesson shows that even evil whispers are from Satan, not from Allah. Knowing this, how will you actively distinguish between whispers to disobey and inspirations to obey? What specific step will you take today to resist Satan's influence?

The Prophetic Principle: Sins Are from Themselves
Author presents Adam's confession and its logical implication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Adam's confession establishes the principle that prophets attributed sins to themselves, refuting the Jabriyya claim that all actions are from Allah.

Core Idea
Prophets held themselves accountable, not Allah.

The author begins by citing the first of many Quranic proofs: Adam's plea. In it, Adam clearly attributes wrongdoing to himself and forgiveness to Allah. This simple distinction contains a powerful refutation of determinism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the explicit distinction between 'ظلمنا أنفسنا' and 'اغفر لنا'.
2
Identify the logical argument
The author argues that if everything were from Allah, then Adam's differentiation between self-blame and divine mercy would be futile. Understand why this is a problem for the Jabriyya.
3
Reflect on the implications
Ask yourself: If Allah created both the sin and the repentance, why would Adam single himself out? This shows the incoherence of absolute determinism.
This connects to the broader debate on human responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما بيان أن الأنبياء عليهم السلام اعترفوا بذلك . ففيه آيات : أ - قال تعالى حكاية عن آدم عليه السلام : ( ربنا ظلمنا أنفسنا . وإن لم تغفر لنا وترحمنا لنكونن من الخاسرين (١) ) فأضاف الظلم والذنب إلى نفسه ، والغفران والرحمة إلى الله تعالى . ولو كان الكل من الله تعالى ، لكان هذا التفصيل والتمييز عبثاً . ب - قال نوح عليه السلام إني أعوذ بك : أن أسألك ما ليس لي به علم (٢) ) ج - قال يعقوب عليه السلام لأولاده : ( بل سولت لكم أنفسكم أمراً (٣) ) د - قال يوسف عليه السلام : ( من بعد أن نزغ الشيطان بيني وبين إخوتي (٤) ) هـ - قال موسى عليه السلام : ( هذا من عمل الشيطان . إنه عدو مضل مبين (٥) ) سماه : عدوا مضلا ، لأنه أوقعه في ذلك العمل ولو كان فاعل ذلك الفعل هو الله تعالى فالعدو والمضل هو الله تعالى و - وقال موسى عليه السلام : رب إني ظلمت نفسي (٦) ) ز - وقال يونس عليه السلام : ( سبحانك . إني كنت من الظالمين (٧) ) فهؤلاء الأنبياء والرسل عليهم السلام اعترفوا بأن الذنب منهم ، وأنهم هم الأمرون بهذه الدلالات . فمن حملها على الله فقد ظاهر بتكذيب الأنبياء
And as for the demonstration that the prophets, peace be upon them, acknowledged that [sins are from themselves]. In it are verses: A. Allah Almighty said, narrating about Adam, peace be upon him: 'Our Lord, we have wronged ourselves, and if You do not forgive us and have mercy upon us, we will surely be among the losers' (1). So he attributed wrongdoing and sin to himself, and forgiveness and mercy to Allah Almighty. Had everything been from Allah Almighty, this differentiation and distinction would be futile. B. Noah, peace be upon him, said: 'I seek refuge in You from asking that of which I have no knowledge' (2). C. Jacob, peace be upon him, said to his sons: 'Rather, your souls have tempted you to something' (3). D. Joseph, peace be upon him, said: 'After Satan had sown discord between me and my brothers' (4). E. Moses, peace be upon him, said: 'This is from the work of Satan. Indeed, he is a manifest enemy, misleader' (5). He called him an enemy and misleader because he caused him to fall into that work. Had the doer of that act been Allah Almighty, then the enemy and misleader would be Allah Almighty. F. And Moses, peace be upon him, said: 'My Lord, I have wronged myself' (6). G. And Jonah, peace be upon him, said: 'Exalted are You! Indeed, I have been of the wrongdoers' (7). So these prophets and messengers, peace be upon them, acknowledged that sin is from them, and that they are the ones who did these indicative actions. Whoever attributes them to Allah has indeed manifested himself as belying the prophets.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage presents another category of proofs: the admissions of the prophets themselves that their sins were from themselves. The author lists seven prophets (Adam, Noah, Jacob, Joseph, Moses, and Jonah) and their statements from the Quran. Each prophet attributed the wrong to himself or to Satan, not to Allah. For Adam, he said 'we have wronged ourselves' and asked for forgiveness. The author argues: if Allah had created the sin, the distinction between self-blame and divine mercy would be pointless. Noah sought refuge from asking without knowledge. Jacob blamed their souls. Joseph attributed discord to Satan. Moses called an act the work of Satan and called Satan a misleader; if Allah were the doer, then Allah would be the misleader. Moses also said 'I have wronged myself'. Jonah said 'I have been of the wrongdoers'. All these show that the prophets held themselves responsible. The author concludes that whoever attributes those sins to Allah has effectively belied the prophets.

Key Terms
الظلم
الذنب
الغفران
الرحمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That prophets' sins were created by Allah and that they were forced to commit them.
Correction: The prophets' own words show they held themselves responsible, not Allah. Adam's distinction would be meaningless if Allah created everything.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what would be the implication if all actions were from Allah, based on Adam's statement?
A) Adam's distinction between self-wrong and divine mercy would be meaningless
B) Adam would not have asked for forgiveness
C) Adam would be a liar
D) Adam's sin would be forgiven automatically

Key Takeaway
Adam's self-attribution of sin and appeal to divine mercy shows that sin is from the human, not from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you instinctively blame Allah's decree or accept your own responsibility? What would change if you truly internalized Adam's confession?
?
Adam, a prophet, immediately acknowledged his wrong. When was the last time you fully owned a mistake without excuse? What keeps you from doing that?
?
If you truly believe that your sins are from you, not from Allah, how would your repentance change? What would you do differently tonight?

Prophets' Confessions: From Noah to Jonah
Author lists six more prophetic admissions and concludes against attributing sin to Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will see how multiple prophets—Noah, Jacob, Joseph, Moses, and Jonah—consistently attributed their errors to themselves or to Satan, not to Allah.

Core Idea
The prophets' consistent self-blame proves human responsibility.

Having established the principle with Adam, the author now presents a chain of prophetic confessions. Each prophet's statement reinforces the same truth: sin originates from the human or from Satan, not from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read each prophetic statement
Read through the Arabic and translation of each verse from Noah to Jonah. Notice the pattern: each prophet either blames himself or Satan.
2
Identify the common pattern
All prophets attribute the sin to themselves (or to Satan) and seek forgiveness from Allah. The author highlights this consistency.
3
Understand the argument from Moses' statement about Satan
Moses calls an act the work of Satan and calls Satan a misleader. The author argues: if Allah were the doer, then Allah would be the misleader, which is impossible.
This is a powerful reductio ad absurdum.
4
Grasp the concluding warning
The author concludes that whoever attributes these sins to Allah has effectively belied the prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما بيان أن الأنبياء عليهم السلام اعترفوا بذلك . ففيه آيات : أ - قال تعالى حكاية عن آدم عليه السلام : ( ربنا ظلمنا أنفسنا . وإن لم تغفر لنا وترحمنا لنكونن من الخاسرين (١) ) فأضاف الظلم والذنب إلى نفسه ، والغفران والرحمة إلى الله تعالى . ولو كان الكل من الله تعالى ، لكان هذا التفصيل والتمييز عبثاً . ب - قال نوح عليه السلام إني أعوذ بك : أن أسألك ما ليس لي به علم (٢) ) ج - قال يعقوب عليه السلام لأولاده : ( بل سولت لكم أنفسكم أمراً (٣) ) د - قال يوسف عليه السلام : ( من بعد أن نزغ الشيطان بيني وبين إخوتي (٤) ) هـ - قال موسى عليه السلام : ( هذا من عمل الشيطان . إنه عدو مضل مبين (٥) ) سماه : عدوا مضلا ، لأنه أوقعه في ذلك العمل ولو كان فاعل ذلك الفعل هو الله تعالى فالعدو والمضل هو الله تعالى و - وقال موسى عليه السلام : رب إني ظلمت نفسي (٦) ) ز - وقال يونس عليه السلام : ( سبحانك . إني كنت من الظالمين (٧) ) فهؤلاء الأنبياء والرسل عليهم السلام اعترفوا بأن الذنب منهم ، وأنهم هم الأمرون بهذه الدلالات . فمن حملها على الله فقد ظاهر بتكذيب الأنبياء
And as for the demonstration that the prophets, peace be upon them, acknowledged that [sins are from themselves]. In it are verses: A. Allah Almighty said, narrating about Adam, peace be upon him: 'Our Lord, we have wronged ourselves, and if You do not forgive us and have mercy upon us, we will surely be among the losers' (1). So he attributed wrongdoing and sin to himself, and forgiveness and mercy to Allah Almighty. Had everything been from Allah Almighty, this differentiation and distinction would be futile. B. Noah, peace be upon him, said: 'I seek refuge in You from asking that of which I have no knowledge' (2). C. Jacob, peace be upon him, said to his sons: 'Rather, your souls have tempted you to something' (3). D. Joseph, peace be upon him, said: 'After Satan had sown discord between me and my brothers' (4). E. Moses, peace be upon him, said: 'This is from the work of Satan. Indeed, he is a manifest enemy, misleader' (5). He called him an enemy and misleader because he caused him to fall into that work. Had the doer of that act been Allah Almighty, then the enemy and misleader would be Allah Almighty. F. And Moses, peace be upon him, said: 'My Lord, I have wronged myself' (6). G. And Jonah, peace be upon him, said: 'Exalted are You! Indeed, I have been of the wrongdoers' (7). So these prophets and messengers, peace be upon them, acknowledged that sin is from them, and that they are the ones who did these indicative actions. Whoever attributes them to Allah has indeed manifested himself as belying the prophets.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage presents another category of proofs: the admissions of the prophets themselves that their sins were from themselves. The author lists seven prophets (Adam, Noah, Jacob, Joseph, Moses, and Jonah) and their statements from the Quran. Each prophet attributed the wrong to himself or to Satan, not to Allah. For Adam, he said 'we have wronged ourselves' and asked for forgiveness. The author argues: if Allah had created the sin, the distinction between self-blame and divine mercy would be pointless. Noah sought refuge from asking without knowledge. Jacob blamed their souls. Joseph attributed discord to Satan. Moses called an act the work of Satan and called Satan a misleader; if Allah were the doer, then Allah would be the misleader. Moses also said 'I have wronged myself'. Jonah said 'I have been of the wrongdoers'. All these show that the prophets held themselves responsible. The author concludes that whoever attributes those sins to Allah has effectively belied the prophets.

Key Terms
الشيطان
العدو المضل
الظالمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Moses' sin was created by Allah because he attributed an act to Satan.
Correction: Moses attributes the act to Satan's misguidance, not to Allah. If Allah were the doer, He would be called the misleader, which is impossible.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what would be the implication if Allah were the doer of the act Moses attributed to Satan?
A) Satan would be innocent
B) Allah would be the misleader
C) Moses would be sinful
D) The act would be good

Key Takeaway
Multiple prophets attributed their sins to themselves or Satan, confirming that sin is not from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you secretly blame Allah's decree to avoid the weight of accountability? After seeing how the prophets owned their faults—blaming themselves or Satan, never Allah—will you stop shifting responsibility and say, 'I have wronged myself'?
?
Jonah cried out from the darkness of the whale: 'Exalted are You! Indeed, I have been of the wrongdoers.' He did not excuse himself. In your own life, when you are caught in a consequence of your sin, do you humbly admit your wrong, or do you search for someone else to blame? What would it take for you to truly say that from your heart right now?
?
Moses called Satan a 'manifest misleader' because he led him into sin. But look at your own patterns: have you ever blamed Allah's predestination for a sin that you knew was your choice? If so, will you repent from that and from this moment forward acknowledge that the sin is from you and not from your Lord?

Learning Objective

Testimonies that Misguidance is Not from God
The author cites Quranic verses and testimonies to prove misguidance is not from God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational and textual evidence from Quran, disbelievers, and Iblis that misguidance (iḍlāl) is not from God, and why attributing sins to God contradicts divine justice.

Core Idea
Multiple witnesses—God, prophets, believers, disbelievers, and even Satan—deny that misguidance comes from God.

In this passage, the author marshals an extraordinary coalition of testimonies: God, the prophets, the believers, the disbelievers, and even Iblis himself. Each witness, from different angles, affirms that misguidance and sins are not from God. By examining these Quranic citations and logical inferences, the author builds a cumulative case that human responsibility remains intact. Let's work through the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the English translation. Notice the flow: from punishment to testimonies to conclusion.
Pay attention to the rhetorical question: 'So if misguidance were from God, then consider what follows.'
2
Identify the testimonies
Find each witness: God's indirect statement, the disbelievers' confession, and Iblis's admission. See how each denies that misguidance is from God.
The disbelievers say: 'None misled us except the criminals.' Iblis says: 'I will surely mislead them.'
3
Analyze the logical challenge
The author presents a conditional: if misguidance were from God, then punishment for it would be unjust. Then he shows that punishment is indeed mentioned, so misguidance cannot be from God.
This is a classic kalam argument from divine justice.
4
Draw the conclusion
The author sums up that all these testimonies—from God, prophets, believers, disbelievers, and Iblis—agree that sins are not from God. Whoever claims otherwise contradicts them all.
This conclusion reinforces human responsibility and divine justice.

Also: God related from the disbelievers that they said: 'And none misled us except the criminals' (1). And as for the proof that Iblis acknowledged that, it is His statement (may He be exalted) narrating from him: 'I will surely take from Your servants an appointed portion' (2). And this is an explicit text that following Satan only occurred because of Satan (12), not because God (may He be exalted) misled them. Satan said: 'And I will surely mislead them' — and this is an acknowledgement from him that misguidance is not from God. Then he said: 'And I will command them so they will alter the creation of God' (3) — and this is explicit in that. Then he said: 'And whoever takes Satan as an ally instead of God' (4) — and this is a threat and warning to whoever does that. And if that were created by God, how would it be appropriate to inflict warning and threat upon it? So it is established by the totality of what we mentioned that the Deity, the prophets, the believers, the disbelievers, and the accursed Iblis all acknowledged that these sins are not from God. So whoever says that they are from God has opposed the truthful, the hypocrite, the Merciful, and Satan.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is a proof by testimonies, arguing that misguidance (al-iḍlāl) cannot be attributed to God. The author begins by citing a Quranic verse (likely from a narration about punishment) and then explains that the mention of punishment is a recompense for their misguidance. He then poses a conditional: if misguidance were from God, then what would follow? This is a rhetorical challenge. Next, he cites the verse (Q. 26:99) where disbelievers say: 'None misled us except the criminals' — thus disbelievers themselves deny that God misled them. Then he turns to Iblis: God narrates that Iblis said: 'I will surely take from Your servants an appointed portion' (Q. 4:118). The author interprets this as Iblis attributing misguidance to himself, not to God. He then quotes Iblis saying: 'And I will surely mislead them' (Q. 4:119) — an admission that it is he who misleads. Iblis also says: 'And I will command them so they will alter the creation of God' (ibid.), again affirming human responsibility. Then he cites the warning: 'Whoever takes Satan as an ally instead of God' (Q. 4:119) — a threat that would be unjust if God were the cause. The author concludes with a logical inference: if God created these sins, threatening the sinner would be inappropriate. Finally, he declares that it is established by all these testimonies that God, prophets, believers, disbelievers, and even Iblis acknowledge that sins are not from God. Therefore, anyone who claims otherwise contradicts all of them.

Correction: The author shows that other verses and testimonies clearly place responsibility on the creature, and that the threat of punishment would be unjust if God were the source of misguidance.

Key Takeaway
The combined testimony of God, prophets, believers, disbelievers, and Iblis establishes that sins are not from God; to claim otherwise contradicts all of them.

Why Human Agency is Necessary for Afterlife Accountability
The author argues that human accountability requires human action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why human agency is essential for divine justice and accountability in the afterlife.

Core Idea
Accountability requires genuine human action; otherwise, divine reproach would be futile.

This passage from Al-Matalibul Aliyah presents a foundational argument linking human free will to divine justice. The author argues that if God were the sole cause of all actions, then holding humans accountable would be irrational. Let's explore this reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the literal translation to grasp the surface meaning.
Pay attention to the key term 'يفصل', which implies active performance by the servant.
2
Identify the conditional argument
The passage is built on an 'if... then...' structure. Identify the condition (if the servant does not perform actions, but God is the doer) and the conclusion (accountability is futile).
3
Reflect on the theological implication
Ask yourself: Why is this argument important for the Islamic discussion on qadar (predestination)? How does it defend human responsibility?
This connects to the broader theme of divine justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع التاسع عشر لهم الآيات الدالة على أحوال أهل القيامة من العقاب والحسنات والثواب والعقاب فلو لم يفصل العبد شيئاً من هذه الأفعال ، بل كان فاعلها هو الله تعالى، كانت محاسبته ومعاتبته عبثاً.
The nineteenth type: verses indicating the states of the people of the Resurrection from punishment, good deeds, reward, and punishment. For if the servant does not perform any of these actions, but rather their doer is God Almighty, then his accounting and reproach would be futile.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage is a concise argument defending human agency in the context of afterlife accountability. The author first identifies the topic: verses describing the states of the people of the Resurrection regarding punishment, good deeds, reward, and punishment. He then presents a logical conditional: if the servant does not produce (يفصل) any of these actions, meaning they are not truly his own doing, but rather God alone is the agent (فاعلها هو الله تعالى), then the very idea of holding him to account (محاسبته) and reproaching him (معاتبته) becomes futile (عبثاً). The argument relies on the principle that rational accountability presupposes genuine authorship of actions. The word 'يفصل' (to perform, to do) is key; it implies a real attribution of the act to the human agent. Thus, the author implicitly defends a position that affirms human free will against a purely predestinarian view that would make God the sole cause of all actions, which would render divine justice meaningless.

Key Terms

فاعلها
محاسبة
معاتبة
عبث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the author is denying God's power, but he is only arguing that accountability requires human agency.
Correction: The author affirms divine power but insists that for justice to be meaningful, humans must be real agents of their actions.

Checkpoint

A) Accountability would be just.
B) Accountability would be futile.
C) Humans would still be responsible.
D) The afterlife would not exist.

Key Takeaway
Without human agency, accountability in the afterlife would be meaningless and unjust.

Refuting the Claim that Allah's Creating Disbelief Negates All Blessings
Author refutes a claim using classification and analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument that refutes the claim that Allah's creation of disbelief leaves no blessing, and why worldly benefits cannot count as genuine blessings in the face of eternal punishment.

Core Idea
Worldly pleasures are like a poisoned sweetmeat — too small to outweigh eternal harm.

This passage presents a powerful refutation of an objection against divine predestination. The opponent argues that if Allah creates disbelief in someone and then punishes them eternally, then Allah has no blessing upon them — a claim that would be absurd. The author responds by distinguishing religious and worldly blessings and showing that even worldly blessings become negligible when compared to eternal punishment. The analogy of poisoned sweetmeat drives the point home.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's claim
Read the first sentence where the opponent's position is stated: 'If Allah created disbelief... then Allah would have no blessing at all upon him.' Notice how the author immediately declares it false.
The claim is the starting point of the argument.
2
Understand the classification of blessings
The author divides blessings into religious and worldly. Identify this classification and note that religious blessings are superior.
3
Follow the reductio on worldly blessings
The author argues that even if worldly blessings exist, they are negligible compared to eternal punishment. Pay attention to the comparisons: drop in the sea, lifespan compared to eternity.
This is the core logical move.
4
Consider the poisoned sweetmeat analogy
Read the analogy of the poisoned sweetmeat. Reflect on why a small pleasure with fatal harm is not considered a blessing.
This makes the abstract argument concrete.
5
Connect back to the refutation
Understand that because the opponent's claim leads to this absurd conclusion (no blessings), the original premise (that Allah creates disbelief) must be false.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع العشرون للقوم
لو أن الله تعالى خلق الكفر في الكافر، وخلقه للنار. ما كان الله نعمة أصلاً .
وهذا باطل فذاك باطل . بيان الملازمة :
إن النعم إما دينية أو دنيوية . ولا شك أن النعم الدينية أفضل وأكمل من النعم الدنيوية . فلو قدرنا أن خالق الكفر هو الله تعالى ، لم يكن له تعالى في خلق الكافر شيء من النعم الدينية . وأما النعم الدنيوية فهي أيضاً على هذا التقدير ، يجب أن تكون معدومة. لأن منافع الإنسان في الدنيا ومضاره فيها ، إذا تقابلا كانت منافعه بالنسبة إلى مضاره كالقطرة في البحر ، ثم إذا قوبل عمر الإنسان بالأبد الذي لا نهاية له ، كان عمره بالنسبة إلى ذلك الأبد كالعدم وإذا كان كذلك ، فلو خلق الله الكفر في الكافر وعذبه عليه أبد الآباد ، كانت المنافع الحاصلة في الدنيا بالنسبة إلى هذه المضار كالقطرة بالنسبة إلى البحار التي لا نهاية لها . ومعلوم : أن مثل هذا لا يعد نعمة ولا منفعة . ألا ترى أن تقديم الخبيص المسموم إلى الإنسان ، لا يعد نعمة . لأن اللذة الحاصلة منه قليلة.
The twentieth type for the people: If Allah, exalted, created disbelief in the disbeliever, and created him for the Fire, then Allah would have no blessing at all upon him. And this is false, so that is false. Explanation of the entailment: Blessings are either religious or worldly. There is no doubt that religious blessings are better and more perfect than worldly blessings. So if we assume that the creator of disbelief is Allah, exalted, then He would have nothing of religious blessings in creating the disbeliever. And as for worldly blessings, also on this supposition, they must be nonexistent. Because the benefits of a human in the world and his harms, if they are compared, his benefits relative to his harms are like a drop in the sea. Then, if the human lifespan is compared to the eternity that has no end, his lifespan relative to that eternity is like non-existence. And if that is so, then if Allah created disbelief in the disbeliever and punished him for it forever and ever, the benefits obtained in the world relative to these harms are like a drop relative to oceans that have no end. And it is known that such a thing is not considered a blessing nor a benefit. Do you not see that presenting poisoned sweetmeat to a person is not considered a blessing, because the pleasure obtained from it is little.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage presents a reductio ad absurdum argument against the claim that if Allah creates disbelief in a person and creates that person for Hellfire, then Allah has no blessing upon him at all. The author first states the opponent's position, then declares it false, and then explains why the entailment leads to absurdity. The argument classifies blessings as either religious or worldly. Religious blessings are clearly superior. If Allah is the creator of disbelief, then He could not have granted any religious blessings to the disbeliever, because disbelief is the opposite of religious good. As for worldly blessings, they might seem possible, but the author argues they too become negligible. He does this by comparing benefits and harms in this world: the ratio is like a drop in the sea. Moreover, human lifespan is infinitely short compared to eternal punishment. Thus, even if worldly benefits existed, they are as nothing next to eternal punishment, so they cannot be called blessings. The author reinforces this with the analogy of a poisoned sweetmeat: the momentary pleasure does not make it a blessing because of the overwhelming harm. This shows that the initial claim is self-defeating, because its implication (no blessings) is absurd, so the original premise (that Allah creates disbelief in the disbeliever) must be false.

Key Terms
النعم (blessings)
النعم الدينية (religious blessings)
النعم الدنيوية (worldly blessings)
الخبيص المسموم (poisoned sweetmeat)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Worldly pleasures are genuine blessings regardless of consequences.
Correction: The author argues that when worldly pleasures are followed by eternal punishment, they are not genuine blessings because the harm outweighs the benefit.

Checkpoint
According to the author's argument, why does the analogy of the poisoned sweetmeat (الخبيص المسموم) support the conclusion?
A) Because the sweetmeat is delicious and therefore a blessing despite the poison.
B) Because the small pleasure of the sweetmeat does not outweigh the fatal harm, so it is not a blessing.
C) Because the sweetmeat is not halal.
D) Because the sweetmeat is presented in a friendly manner.

Key Takeaway
Allah's creation of disbelief in a person does not negate all blessings because religious blessings are separate, and worldly blessings are insignificant compared to eternal punishment, as illustrated by the poisoned sweetmeat analogy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you pursuing any worldly pleasure right now that, if you were honest with yourself, you know is pulling you away from Allah? Imagine that pleasure as a piece of poisoned sweetmeat—does the momentary taste justify the eternal harm? What will you do about it today?
?
The author says religious blessings are far better than worldly ones. Have you truly prioritized seeking religious blessings—like knowledge, sincere worship, and closeness to Allah—over chasing temporary comforts? If not, what is holding you back, and will you commit to shifting your focus starting now?
?
If you were to stand before Allah tomorrow, would the worldly blessings you have cherished be enough to outweigh your sins? Or have you been deceived by the drop of pleasure while ignoring the ocean of consequence? Make a pact with yourself to re-evaluate your choices this week and turn to Allah for forgiveness and guidance.

The Core Argument: Life as the Foundation of Blessings
Author states the proof and introduces life as the source of all blessings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of the argument that if God created disbelief, He would have no blessings for the disbeliever, and how the Quran establishes life as the origin of all blessings.

Core Idea
Without life, no blessing can be enjoyed — life is the root of all gratitude.

This passage opens with a powerful logical move: if God were the creator of disbelief, then disbelievers would deserve no blessings. But the Quran shows that blessings begin with life itself, which all humans possess. Let's trace this reasoning and see how the author anchors the entire argument in the Qur’anic verse about life.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the passage carefully to catch the logical flow from the conditional premise to the foundation of blessings.
2
Identify the conditional argument
Notice how the author states 'if disbelief were created by God, then no blessings' — this is a contradiction he wants to prove false.
3
Examine the role of life
The author claims life is the origin of all blessings. Reflect on why that is: without life, no benefit.
This connects to the Quranic verse 'How can you disbelieve in Allah? And you were dead and He gave you life.'
4
Trace the Quranic sequence
See how the author uses three consecutive verses to show God's blessings: life, creation of earth, then heavens.
This structure shows the order of blessings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالنسبة إلى المضار الحاصلة . فكذا ههنا . فثبت : أنه لو كان حصول الكفر بخلق الله تعالى ، لم يكن الله تعالى في حق الكافر شيء من النعم البتة . وإنما قلنا : إن الله نعمة في حق الكافر، بل نعماً ، لا حد لها ولا حصر ، ذكره الله تعالى في كتابه على الترتيب المعقول . وذلك لأن أصل جميع النعم هو الحياة . فإنه لولا الحياة لما حصل الانتفاع. فكانت الحياة أصلاً لجميع النعم . فلهذا السبب ابتدأ الله تعالى بذكره فقال : كيف تكفرون بالله . وكنتم أمواتاً فأحياكم . ثم قال : هو الذي خلق لكم ما في الأرض جميعاً . ثم قال : ثم استوى إلى السماء فسواهن سبع سموات . وأيضاً : قال : يا بني إسرائيل اذكروا نعمتي التي أنعمت عليكم . وهذا تصريح بأن الله تعالى قد أنعم على الكفار . وقال في قصة إبليس : ولا تجد أكثرهم شاكرين . ولو لم تكن عليهم النعم من الله ، ما كان لهذا القول فائدة . وقال حاكياً عن موسى : أغير الله أبغيكم إنها . وهو فضلكم على العالمين . وقال في سورة النحل : والأنعام خلقها . لكم فيها دفء ومنافع ومنها تأكلون . ولا شك أن هذا مذكور في معرض تعديد النعم . ثم قال : هو الذي أنزل من السماء ماء . لكم منه شراب ، ومنه شجر . إلى قوله : وإن تعدوا نعمة الله لا تحصوها . وهذه الآيات دالة على أن نعم الله واصلة إلى جميع الخلق . فثبت : أنه تعالى لو خلق الكفر في الكافر، لما كان له عليه نعمة . وثبت بهذه الآيات : أن نعم الله واصلة إلى الكافر والمؤمن . وهذا يدل على أنه ليس خالقا للكفر في حق الكافر .
With respect to the harms that occur, so here likewise. So it is established: if the occurrence of disbelief were by the creation of Allah, then Allah would not have any blessing whatsoever for the disbeliever. And we only say: Allah has a blessing for the disbeliever, rather blessings, without limit or count, which Allah mentioned in His book in a rational order. That is because the origin of all blessings is life. For if there were no life, no benefit would be obtained. So life is the origin of all blessings. For this reason Allah began His mention of it, saying: 'How can you disbelieve in Allah? And you were dead and He gave you life.' Then He said: 'He is the One who created for you all that is on the earth.' Then He said: 'Then He turned to the sky and made them seven heavens.' Also He said: 'O Children of Israel, remember My blessing which I bestowed upon you.' And this is a declaration that Allah has bestowed blessings upon the disbelievers. And He said in the story of Iblis: 'And you will not find most of them grateful.' And if the blessings from Allah were not upon them, this statement would have no benefit. And relating from Moses: 'Shall I seek for you a god other than Allah while He has favored you over the worlds?' And He said in Surah an-Nahl: 'And the cattle He created; for you in them is warmth and benefits, and from them you eat.' And there is no doubt that this is mentioned in the context of counting blessings. Then He said: 'He is the One who sends down rain from the sky; from it you drink, and from it come trees' until His saying: 'And if you count the blessings of Allah, you cannot enumerate them.' And these verses indicate that the blessings of Allah reach all creatures. So it is established: if He had created disbelief in the disbeliever, then He would have no blessing upon him. And by these verses it is established that the blessings of Allah reach the disbeliever and the believer. And this indicates that He is not the creator of disbelief with respect to the disbeliever.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage presents a theological proof by contradiction: if God were the direct creator of disbelief (kufr) in a person, then that person would deserve no blessings from God, because disbelief is the greatest sin and ingratitude. However, the Quran repeatedly affirms that God bestows countless blessings upon all people, including disbelievers, such as life, sustenance, health, and the benefits of the earth and sky. The author lists several verses to show that God's blessings are universal and begin with life itself, which is the foundation for all other blessings. Since disbelievers do enjoy these blessings, it follows that God does not create their disbelief—otherwise He would be blessing them while simultaneously deserving punishment, which is incoherent. Therefore, the argument concludes that God cannot be the creator of disbelief in the disbeliever.

Key Terms
نعم (blessings)
كفر (disbelief)
خلق (creation)
حياة (life)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God creates all actions, including disbelief, then He can still bless the disbeliever without contradiction.
Correction: The author argues that if God created the very act of disbelief which is the ultimate ingratitude, then there would be no basis for blessing that person, because blessing presupposes some good in the recipient. However, since we observe blessings, God cannot be the creator of disbelief.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the foundational blessing that underlies all others?
A) Wealth
B) Health
C) Life
D) Faith

Key Takeaway
The argument that disbelievers possess life proves they have blessings, contradicting the idea that God created their disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You now know that life is the origin of every blessing. When you complain about what you lack, do you ever pause to thank Allah for the breath in your lungs? How can you make gratitude for your existence a daily habit, starting right now?
?
The passage shows that even a disbeliever has countless blessings. As a believer, are you more grateful than a disbeliever? Or have you taken the gift of life for granted? What will you do today to remind yourself that life itself is an undeserved mercy?
?
If Allah were to create your disbelief, you would have no blessings at all. Yet He gives you life and countless favors. How does this truth move you to draw closer to Him in thankfulness and obedience? Write one concrete action you will take today to express your gratitude.

Quranic Witnesses to Universal Blessings
Author cites Quranic verses proving blessings for disbelievers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will recognize how multiple Quranic verses explicitly state that God's blessings extend to disbelievers as well as believers.

Core Idea
The Quran repeatedly affirms that God’s blessings reach all people, including those who disbelieve.

After establishing life as the foundational blessing, the author brings a series of Quranic verses that declare God's blessings upon all people, including the disbelievers. These verses serve as direct evidence against the notion that God created disbelief, because blessings are incompatible with God being the source of the ultimate ingratitude.

Guided Path

Read the verses one by one
Each verse is cited by the author to show a different aspect of God’s blessings to all, including disbelievers.
2
Note the contexts

The author uses both specific and general verses.
3
Reflect on the logical implication
Ask yourself: Why would the Quran remind disbelievers of blessings if those blessings were not from God?
If God were the creator of their disbelief, He would not bless them in this way.

Conclusion: God Does Not Create Disbelief
Author concludes that God does not create disbelief based on universal blessings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the evidence of universal blessings leads to the conclusion that God does not create disbelief, and how this protects the divine attribute of grace.

Core Idea
Since God blesses disbelievers, He cannot be the creator of their disbelief.

The author now draws the final conclusion from all the Quranic evidence: God’s blessings reach both believers and disbelievers. If He had created disbelief in the disbeliever, He would not have blessed him. Therefore, God is not the creator of disbelief. This conclusion affirms that human choice plays a role in the acquisition of faith and disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the concluding lines
The author repeats the conclusion and ties it to the earlier argument.
2
Understand the logical connection
The blessings prove God's grace; disbelief cannot be from the same source that gives those blessings.
3
Reflect on the implication
This conclusion implies human responsibility for disbelief, while God's attributes of generosity and justice remain intact.

Divine Decree
intermediate
8 min
God's Universal Blessings Prove He Does Not Create Disbelief
Author cites Quranic verses to prove that God's blessings reach all, concluding He does not create disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic evidence of God's universal blessings leads to the conclusion that God does not create disbelief, and how apparent scriptural conflicts are resolved by rational proofs.

Core Idea
God's universal blessings prove He does not create disbelief.

In this passage, the author builds a cumulative case from the Quran, showing that God's favors extend to both believers and disbelievers. From this, he draws a theological conclusion: God cannot be the creator of disbelief, because that would contradict His blessings. Then he anticipates an objection — that other verses seem to say the opposite — and provides a methodological principle: when scriptures appear to conflict, rational proofs are the final arbiter.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic citations
Notice each verse the author cites and how it describes God's blessings.
The verses are from different surahs, all emphasizing universal favor.
2
Follow the logical deduction
The author argues: if God created disbelief, the disbeliever would have no favor from God. But the verses show favors upon all. Therefore, God does not create disbelief.
3
Understand the resolution of conflict
The author acknowledges there are also verses supporting the opposing view. He says the solution is to rely on rational proofs, which are decisive.
This is a key methodological move in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خلق لكم ما في الأرض جميعاً ثم ذكر بعده : أنه تعالى قصد إلى السموات وساها تسوية مطابقة لمصالح العباد فقال : ثم استوى إلى السماء فسواهن سبع سموات وأيضاً : قال : يا بني إسرائيل اذكروا نعمتي التي أنعمت عليكم وهذا تصريح بأن الله تعالى قد أنعم على الكفار . وقال في قصة إبليس : ولا تجد أكثرهم شاكرين ولو لم تكن عليهم النعم من الله ، ما كان لهذا القول فائدة وقال حاكياً عن موسى : أغير الله أبغيكم إنها وهو فضلكم على العالمين ؟ وقال في سورة النحل : والأنعام خلقها لكم فيها دفء ومنافع ومنها تأكلون ولا شك أن هذا مذكور في معرض تعديد النعم . ثم قال : هو الذي أنزل من السماء ماء لكم منه شراب ومنه شجر إلى قوله : وإن تعدوا نعمة الله لا تحصوها وهذه الآيات دالة على أن نعم الله واصلة إلى جميع الخلق . فثبت : أنه تعالى لو خلق الكفر في الكافر لما كان له عليه نعمة . وثبت بهذه الآيات : أن نعم الله واصلة إلى الكافر والمؤمن . وهذا يدل على أنه ليس خالقا للكفر في حق الكافر . واعلم : أن من وقف على هذه الوجوه العشرين التي لخصناها للقوم أمكنه الاستدلال بكل آية من آيات القرآن واعلم : أن المعتمد في الجواب أن نقول : الآيات الدالة على مذهبنا أيضاً كثيرة جداً . ولما تعارضت تلك الآيات بهذه الآيات وجب الرجوع فيها إلى الدلائل العقلية التي عولنا عليها فإنها باهرة قوية لا شك فيها ولا شبهة والله ولي التوفيق
He created for you all that is on the earth. Then He mentioned afterward that He, exalted, intended the heavens and fashioned them with a fashioning suitable for the interests of servants, saying: 'Then He turned to the heaven and fashioned them seven heavens.' And also He said: 'O Children of Israel, remember My favor which I bestowed upon you.' And this is a declaration that God, exalted, has bestowed favor upon the disbelievers. And He said in the story of Iblis: 'And you will not find most of them grateful.' And were it not that favors from God are upon them, this statement would have no benefit. And he narrated from Moses: 'Would I seek for you a god other than God while He has favored you over the worlds?' And He said in Surat an-Nahl: 'And the cattle He created them; in them there is warmth and benefits and from them you eat.' There is no doubt that this is mentioned in the context of enumerating favors. Then He said: 'It is He who sends down from the sky water; for you from it is drink and from it is trees' until His saying: 'And if you count the favor of God you cannot enumerate it.' And these verses indicate that God's favors reach all creatures. So it is established: if He, exalted, had created disbelief in the disbeliever, then there would be no favor from Him upon him. And it is established by these verses that God's favors reach the disbeliever and the believer. And this indicates that He is not the creator of disbelief with respect to the disbeliever. And know: whoever comes across these twenty aspects that we have summarized for the people can use every verse of the Quran as evidence. And know: the relied-upon answer is to say: the verses indicating our doctrine are also very many. And when those verses conflict with these verses, it becomes necessary to refer back to the rational proofs that we have relied upon, for they are brilliant and strong, with no doubt or suspicion in them. And God is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage presents a cumulative Quranic argument followed by a methodological principle. The author first cites a series of verses demonstrating that God's blessings encompass both believers and disbelievers, then draws the theological conclusion that God does not create disbelief in the disbeliever. The reasoning is: if God had created disbelief in the disbeliever, then that disbeliever would not be receiving any favor from God, because disbelief is the opposite of gratitude. Yet the Quran repeatedly emphasizes God's favors upon all people, including disbelievers (e.g., the verses about creation, the story of Iblis, Moses' speech, and various enumerations of blessings). Therefore, the author concludes that God is not the creator of disbelief. After this, he notes that whoever understands these twenty aspects (presumably arguments summarized earlier) can use every Qur'anic verse as evidence. He then addresses a potential conflict: there are also many verses supporting the opposing view (that God creates all things, including disbelief). In such cases of scriptural apparent contradiction, the author asserts that one must resort to rational proofs (al-adilla al-'aqliyya), which he deems decisive and beyond doubt. The passage ends with a prayer for divine assistance.

Key Terms
خلق الله للكفر
نعم الله
الدلائل العقلية
تعارض الآيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's blessings are exclusive to believers; He may create disbelief in disbelievers without contradiction.
Correction: The Quran explicitly states God's favors reach disbelievers too. If God created their disbelief, they would have no favor from Him. Therefore, God cannot be the creator of disbelief.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the fact that God's blessings reach both the disbeliever and the believer indicate?
A) God loves the disbeliever equally
B) God is not the creator of disbelief in the disbeliever
C) The disbeliever will be rewarded for his deeds
D) The verses about blessings are abrogated

Key Takeaway
God's universal blessings in the Quran prove that He does not create disbelief, and when verses seem to conflict, rational proofs must decide.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you come across Quranic verses that seem to conflict, are you quick to pick a side without seeking a deeper resolution? Will you now commit to the hard work of rational inquiry (using your God-given intellect) rather than settling for comfortable oversimplifications?
?
If every moment and blessing is a sign that God's favor reaches you—even when you are ungrateful—what should change in how you wake up each morning and use your breath?

Divine Decree
beginner
5 min
The First Argument: Disbelief Cannot Be from Allah's Decree
First proof that kufr and fisq are not from Allah's decree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first rational proof that disbelief and sin are not created or decreed by Allah, based on the obligation to be pleased with His decree.

Core Idea
If evil were decreed, we would have to be pleased with it—but we cannot be.

This lesson presents the first of several proofs used by a rationalist school (likely the Mu'tazila) to argue that disbelief and sin are not from Allah's decree. The author builds a conditional syllogism: if kufr were decreed, it would demand satisfaction; since satisfaction with evil is impermissible, kufr cannot be decreed. The proof draws on consensus, the Quran, and a prophetic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Understand the conditional syllogism
Read the first part of the source: 'If disbelief and sin occurred by Allah's creation and decree, then being pleased with it would be obligatory. But being pleased with it is not permissible...' Notice the logical structure: 'If P, then Q; not Q; therefore not P.'
This is a classic proof by contrapositive.
2
Examine the premise of obligation
The author then explains the implication: everything that is by Allah's decree must be pleased with. This is claimed to be agreed upon by the community. Reflect on why this premise is crucial to the argument.
3
Study the Quranic evidence
Read the verse from Surah al-Ahzab (33:36) which says believers have no choice when Allah and His Messenger decree a matter. Consider how this supports the obligation of acceptance.
4
Reflect on the hadith evidence
Read the hadith from Sa'd ibn Malik (Abu Sa'id al-Khudri) that lists being pleased with Allah's decree as a sign of happiness and displeasure as a sign of misery. Notice how this reinforces the premise.
The hadith is incomplete in this excerpt but conveys the key idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم : أن كل ما ورد من الأخبار ، من الأمر والنهي ، والمدح والذم والثواب والعقاب ، والترغيب والترهيب، فالقوم يحتجون به. وتقريره على الوجه المذكور في الدلائل القرآنية
ثم بعد هذا يتمسكون بوجوه أخرى :
الحجة الأولى : لو كان الكفر والفسق حاصلا بتخليق الله تعالى وقضائه لوجب الرضا به. لكن الرضا به لا يجوز ، فوجب أن لا يكون بتخليق الله ولا بقضائه . بيان الملازمة :
إن كل ما كان بقضاء الله ، فإنه يجب الرضا به ، فذلك مجمع عليه بين الأمة . ثم نقول : الدليل عليه أيضاً : القرآن والخبر والأثر .
أما القرآن : فقوله تعالى : ( وما كان لمؤمن ولا مؤمنة إذا قضى الله ورسوله أمراً أن يكون لهم الخيرة من أمرهم )
وأما الأخبار فكثيرة : أحدها: ما روى سعد بن مالك قال : قال رسول الله : « من سعادة ابن آدم استخارة الله ، ومن سعادة ابن آدم رضاه بما قضى الله ، ومن شقاوة ابن آدم تركه استخارة الله ، ومن شقاوة ابن آدم سخطه
Know: that every report that has come, of command and prohibition, praise and blame, reward and punishment, encouragement and deterrence, the people (al-qawm) argue by it. And its presentation is in the manner mentioned in the Quranic proofs. Then after this they adhere to other aspects: The first proof: If disbelief (kufr) and sin (fisq) occurred by the creation (takhliq) of Allah Most High and His decree (qada'), then being pleased (al-rida) with it would be obligatory. But being pleased with it is not permissible, so it must be that it is not by the creation of Allah nor by His decree. Explanation of the implication: Indeed, everything that is by the decree of Allah, then being pleased with it is obligatory, for that is agreed upon by the community (umma). Then we say: the proof for it also: the Quran, the hadith, and the athar. As for the Quran: His statement Most High: (It is not for a believing man or a believing woman, when Allah and His Messenger have decreed a matter, that they should have any choice in their matter). As for the reports, they are many: one of them: what Sa'd ibn Malik narrated: he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'From the happiness of the son of Adam is his seeking guidance (istikharah) from Allah, and from the happiness of the son of Adam is his being pleased with what Allah has decreed for him, and from the misery of the son of Adam is his abandonment of seeking guidance from Allah, and from the misery of the son of Adam is his anger.'
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage presents the first proof in a series of arguments that disbelief and sin are not created or decreed by Allah. The author begins by noting that the group (presumably the Mu'tazila or a rationalist school) uses all types of revealed reports—commands, prohibitions, praise, blame, reward, punishment, encouragement, and deterrence—as evidence, as explained in the section on Quranic proofs. Then, after that, they resort to other arguments. The first argument is a conditional syllogism: If kufr and fisq were brought about by Allah's creation and decree, then it would be obligatory to be pleased with them. However, being pleased with them is not permissible (because they are evil and displeasing to Allah). Therefore, kufr and fisq cannot be from Allah's creation or decree. The author then explains the implication: the premise that 'everything that is by Allah's decree must be pleased with' is agreed upon by the Muslim community. To support this premise, he cites the Quran (33:36) which indicates that believers have no choice when Allah and His Messenger decree a matter, implying they must accept it. He also cites a hadith from Sa'd ibn Malik (Abu Sa'id al-Khudri) that lists being pleased with Allah's decree as a sign of happiness, and displeasure with it as a sign of misery. Thus, the argument uses consensus, Quran, and hadith to establish that if an evil like kufr were decreed, one would have to be pleased with it, but since it is impermissible to be pleased with evil, it cannot be decreed.

فسق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the argument claims that everything decreed is good or that being pleased with evil is actually required.
Correction: The argument does not claim that evil is good; rather, it uses the agreed-upon obligation to be pleased with Allah's decree to show that evil cannot be attributed to His decree, because one cannot be pleased with evil.

Checkpoint
According to the first argument presented, what is the logical consequence if disbelief (kufr) were created and decreed by Allah?
A) It would not be sinful.
B) One would have to be pleased with it.
C) It would be impossible for humans to commit it.
D) It would be an act of worship.

Key Takeaway
The first argument against ascribing disbelief and sin to Allah's decree is that it would obligate being pleased with evil, which is impermissible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever catch yourself thinking, 'It was meant to be' or 'Allah willed it'? How does this lesson challenge that excuse? What will you do this week to take full ownership of your choices and turn to Allah in repentance instead of attributing wrongdoing to His decree?
?
The hadith says being pleased with Allah's decree is a sign of happiness, and displeasure a sign of misery. Think of one area in your life where you have been angry or resentful about Allah's decree—perhaps a loss, a trial, or a situation you wanted to change. What would it practically mean for you to truly be pleased with that decree? What is holding you back from that contentment?
?
If this argument proves that evil cannot be from Allah's decree, then where does evil come from? How does your answer affect how you live your daily life? Commit to one concrete action you will take today to resist evil, knowing that it is your responsibility—not Allah's decree—to choose good.

Divine Decree
intermediate

The Qadariyya's First Proof: Structure and Entailment
Statement of the Qadariyya's first proof and its logical structure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of the Qadariyya's first argument against divine decree of kufr, including the key entailment (mulazama) they propose.

Core Idea
If kufr were from God's decree, it would demand approval; but it doesn't, so it isn't.

This lesson introduces the first of several proofs used by the Qadariyya to argue that disbelief cannot be created or decreed by Allah. The argument rests on a simple but powerful logical implication: if something is from God's decree, then being pleased with it is obligatory. Since being pleased with disbelief is not permissible, disbelief cannot be from God's decree. We will examine the initial statement of this proof and its internal logic.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic text of the first proof carefully. Then read the English translation to grasp the core argument.
Notice how the proof is introduced as 'al-hujjah al-ula' (the first proof).
2
Identify the conditional statement
Find the 'if...then' structure: If kufr and fisq are by God's creation and decree, then being pleased with them is wajib (obligatory).
This is the major premise of the argument.
3
Recognize the entailment
The argument uses a 'mulazama' (entailment) to connect the major premise to the conclusion. Understand that the conclusion follows logically from the premises.
4
Ask: What is the conclusion?
The conclusion is that kufr and fisq cannot be from God's creation or decree. State it in your own words.
This directly opposes the Ash'ari position that all actions are created by Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم : أن كل ما ورد من الأخبار ، من الأمر والنهي ، والمدح والذم والثواب والعقاب ، والترغيب والترهيب، فالقوم يحتجون به. وتقريره على الوجه المذكور في الدلائل القرآنية ثم بعد هذا يتمسكون بوجوه أخرى : الحجة الأولى : لو كان الكفر والفسق حاصلا بتخليق الله تعالى وقضائه لوجب الرضا به. لكن الرضا به لا يجوز ، فوجب أن لا يكون بتخليق الله ولا بقضائه . بيان الملازمة : إن كل ما كان بقضاء الله ، فإنه يجب الرضا به ، فذلك مجمع عليه بين الأمة . ثم نقول : الدليل عليه أيضاً : القرآن والخبر والأثر . أما القرآن : فقوله تعالى : ( وما كان لمؤمن ولا مؤمنة إذا قضى الله ورسوله أمراً أن يكون لهم الخيرة من أمرهم ) وأما الأخبار فكثيرة : أحدها: ما روى سعد بن مالك قال : قال رسول الله : « من سعادة ابن آدم استخارة الله ، ومن سعادة ابن آدم رضاه بما قضى الله ، ومن شقاوة ابن آدم تركه استخارة الله ، ومن شقاوة ابن آدم سخطه بما قضى الله . وثانيها : ما روى عبد الله بن عمر : أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يقول: «اللهم إني أسألك الصحة والعفة والأمانة وحسن الخلق والرضاء بالقدر » وثالثها : ما روى عبد الله بن شداد قال : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : « اللهم رضني بقضائك ، وبارك لي في قدرك ، حتى لا أحب تأخير ما عجلت ولا تعجيل ما أخرت » ورابعها : إن من مشاهير الأخبار الربانية : أنه : حكى عن رب العزة أنه يقول : « ومن لم يرض بقضائي ، فليطلب رباً سواي ) . وأما الآثار فكثيرة : أحدها : قال أبو الدرداء : « المروءة أربع خلال : الصبر للحكم ، والرضاء بالقدر ، والإخلاص في التوكل ، والاستسلام للموت ، وعنه أيضاً أنه قال : « إن الله إذا قضى قضاء ، أحب أن يرضى بقضائه ، وثانيها : عن عمران بن حصين أنه قال : ثلاث يدرك بهن العبد رغائب الدنيا والآخرة : الصبر عند البلاء ، والرضا بالقدر ، والدعاء في الرخاء ، وثالثها : روى محمد بن كعب : أن موسى عليه السلام قال : « أي ربي أي خلقك أعظم ذنباً ؟ ، قال : « الذي يتهمني ، قال : « أي ربي ، وهل يتهمك أحد ؟ ، قال : ( نعم الذي يستخيرني ولا يرضى بقضائي ، ورابعها : قيل فيها أوحي الله تعالى إلى داود عليه السلام : « يا داود إنك لن تلقاني بعمل هو أرضى لي عنك ، ولا أحط لوزرك من الرضا بقضائي ) . فثبت بهذه الوجوه : أنه لو كان الكفر بقضاء الله لكان الرضا به واجباً وأما بيان أنه لا يجوز الرضا بالكفر والعصيان : فهذا أيضاً مجمع عليه بين الأمة . ثم الدليل عليه : القرآن والخبر . أما القرآن : فهو أن الظالم يجب لعنه . لقوله تعالى : ( ألا لعنة الله على الظالمين ) وذلك ينافي وجوب الرضا بظلمه . وأيضاً : فالأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر واجب بأقصى الوجوه . وذلك يمنع من وجوب حصول الرضا بالكفر والفسق
Know: that whatever reports have come, of command and prohibition, praise and blame, reward and punishment, encouragement and discouragement, the people argue with them. And its explanation is according to the way mentioned in the Quranic proofs. Then after this they adhere to other aspects: The first proof: If disbelief and wickedness occurred by the creation of God Almighty and His decree, then being pleased with them would be obligatory. But being pleased with them is not permissible, so it must be that they are not by the creation of God nor by His decree. Explanation of the entailment: Everything that is by the decree of God, then being pleased with it is obligatory, for that is agreed upon by the community. Then we say: The proof of it also is the Quran, the report, and the tradition. As for the Quran: His saying Almighty (And it is not for a believing man or a believing woman, when God and His Messenger have decreed a matter, that they should have any choice in their matter). As for reports, many: One of them: what Sa'd ibn Malik narrated, said: the Messenger of God said: 'Among the happiness of the son of Adam is his seeking guidance from God, and among the happiness of the son of Adam is his being pleased with what God decrees, and among the misery of the son of Adam is his abandoning seeking guidance from God, and among the misery of the son of Adam is his displeasure with what God decrees.' Second: what Abdullah ibn Umar narrated: that the Messenger of God used to say: 'O God, I ask You for health, chastity, trustworthiness, good character, and being pleased with destiny.' Third: what Abdullah ibn Shaddad narrated, said: the Messenger of God used to say: 'O God, make me pleased with Your decree, and bless me in Your destiny, so that I do not love delay of what You have hastened nor hastening of what You have delayed.' Fourth: among the famous divine reports: that it is narrated from the Lord of Might that He says: 'Whoever is not pleased with My decree, let him seek a lord other than Me.' As for traditions, many: One of them: Abu Darda said: 'Manliness consists of four traits: patience under judgement, being pleased with destiny, sincerity in trust, and surrender to death.' And also from him: 'When God decrees a decree, He loves that one be pleased with His decree.' Second: from Imran ibn Husain: 'Three things by which the servant attains the desires of this world and the Hereafter: patience at calamity, being pleased with destiny, and supplication in prosperity.' Third: Muhammad ibn Kab narrated that Moses said: 'O my Lord, which of Your creation is greatest in sin?' He said: 'The one who accuses Me.' He said: 'O my Lord, does anyone accuse You?' He said: 'Yes, the one who seeks guidance from Me and is not pleased with My decree.' Fourth: it is said in revelation to David: 'O David, you will not meet Me with a deed more pleasing to Me from you, nor more lightening of your burden, than being pleased with My decree.' So it is established by these aspects that if disbelief were by the decree of God, then being pleased with it would be obligatory. As for the explanation that being pleased with disbelief and disobedience is not permissible: this also is agreed upon by the community. Then the proof of it is the Quran and the report. As for the Quran: that the wrongdoer must be cursed, because of His saying Almighty: (Beware, the curse of God is upon the wrongdoers). And that contradicts the obligation of being pleased with his wrongdoing. Also: commanding good and forbidding evil is obligatory in the strongest manner. And that prevents the obligation of obtaining being pleased with disbelief and wickedness.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage presents the first proof (al-hujjah al-ula) used by a group referred to as 'al-qawm' (the people) — likely the Qadariyya or Mu'tazila who deny that God creates human actions, particularly evil ones. They argue that if disbelief (kufr) and wickedness (fisq) were created by God and decreed by Him, then being pleased (rida) with them would be obligatory. However, being pleased with them is not permissible (la yajuz), so they cannot be from God's creation or decree. The argument is structured as an entailment (mulazama): they first prove the major premise — that everything from God's decree requires being pleased with it. They claim this is agreed upon (mujma' 'alayh) by the community. Then they support this premise with evidence from the Quran, reports (akhbar), and traditions (athar). They cite Quran 33:36, several hadith about the virtue of being pleased with God's decree, and sayings of the salaf (e.g., Abu Darda, Imran ibn Husain) and prophetic traditions emphasizing contentment with divine decree. After establishing the major premise, they affirm the minor premise: that being pleased with disbelief and disobedience is not permissible. This too is claimed to be agreed upon, and they support it with Quranic evidence that wrongdoers are cursed (Quran 7:44) and the obligation of commanding good and forbidding evil, which precludes being pleased with evil. The overall argument is a classic Qadariyya proof that since God's decree demands acceptance, and evil cannot be accepted, evil cannot be from God's decree. The text presents the argument without immediate refutation here.

Key Terms
قضاء
رضا
تخليق
الكفر
الفسق
الملازمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Qadariyya argument proves that Allah cannot decree evil actions at all.
Correction: The argument only proves that if decreeing kufr would require divine approval of evil, but the Ash'ari position distinguishes between decree (qada') and approval (rida). Allah decrees without being pleased with the moral evil itself.

Checkpoint
What is the logical structure of the Qadariyya's first proof?
A) If kufr is from Allah's decree, then rida is optional; but rida is forbidden; so kufr is not from decree.
B) If kufr is from Allah's decree, then rida is obligatory; but rida with kufr is not permissible; so kufr is not from decree.
C) If kufr is from Allah's decree, then rida is prohibited; but rida with kufr is obligatory; so kufr is from decree.
D) If kufr is from human free will, then rida is obligatory; but rida is not permissible; so kufr is from decree.

Key Takeaway
The Qadariyya's first proof is a conditional argument: since being pleased with disbelief is impermissible, disbelief cannot be part of Allah's decree.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial or see evil in the world, do you find yourself thinking that if God decreed it, then He must approve of it, and thus you feel justified in complaining or being upset? How can you change that reaction in light of the distinction between decree and approval that this lesson highlights?
?
The Qadariyya argued that since we must not be pleased with disbelief, it cannot be from Allah's decree. But have you ever used a similar logic to reject something about yourself—e.g., 'God couldn't have willed this sin in me because I hate it'—and thus denied His sovereignty? What does this lesson teach you about the relationship between your dislike of sin and God's decree?
?
If being pleased with disbelief is impermissible, then how do you reconcile the fact that disbelief occurs in the world with the belief that everything is by Allah's decree? Does your heart rest on the Ash'ari understanding that decree does not imply approval, or do you secretly hold the Qadariyya's view that you must deny the decree to avoid approval? Be honest: which position brings you closer to God in submission?
