Divine Decree
intermediate
8 min
Evidence for the Major Premise: Rida with Decree is Obligatory
Qadariyya evidence for the duty to be pleased with divine decree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the textual evidence the Qadariyya use to support their claim that everything from Allah's decree must be met with rida (pleasure), as part of their argument against divine decree of kufr.

Core Idea
The obligation to accept divine decree is supported by Quran, hadith, and traditions of the salaf.

Having stated the logical form, the Qadariyya now defend the key premise: that whatever is from Allah's decree requires being pleased with it. They claim this is agreed upon by the community and then bring extensive evidence from the Quran, numerous hadiths, and sayings of the Companions and earlier prophets. This lesson will examine that evidence to understand how they build their case.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage evidence
Read the Arabic and translation of the section starting from 'Bayān al-mulāzama' (Explanation of the entailment).
Notice they claim ijma' (consensus) on this point first.
2
Categorize the three types of evidence
Identify the three categories: Quran (Quran 33:36), reports (akhbar, four hadiths), and traditions (athar, four sayings). List each one.
This shows the comprehensive nature of their proof.
3
Analyze the Quranic verse
Read the verse (33:36) and understand how it implies no choice after God's decree, thus requiring acceptance.
4
Review the hadiths
Go through each of the four hadiths cited. Note the common theme of rida with qada' (decree).
The hadiths include statements from the Prophet about happiness and misery tied to acceptance of decree.
5
Review the athar
Look at the sayings of Abu Darda, Imran ibn Husain, and the stories of Musa and Dawud. Notice how they emphasize rida with divine decree.
These reinforce the point from earlier generations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم : أن كل ما ورد من الأخبار ، من الأمر والنهي ، والمدح والذم والثواب والعقاب ، والترغيب والترهيب، فالقوم يحتجون به. وتقريره على الوجه المذكور في الدلائل القرآنية ثم بعد هذا يتمسكون بوجوه أخرى : الحجة الأولى : لو كان الكفر والفسق حاصلا بتخليق الله تعالى وقضائه لوجب الرضا به. لكن الرضا به لا يجوز ، فوجب أن لا يكون بتخليق الله ولا بقضائه . بيان الملازمة : إن كل ما كان بقضاء الله ، فإنه يجب الرضا به ، فذلك مجمع عليه بين الأمة . ثم نقول : الدليل عليه أيضاً : القرآن والخبر والأثر . أما القرآن : فقوله تعالى : ( وما كان لمؤمن ولا مؤمنة إذا قضى الله ورسوله أمراً أن يكون لهم الخيرة من أمرهم ) وأما الأخبار فكثيرة : أحدها: ما روى سعد بن مالك قال : قال رسول الله : « من سعادة ابن آدم استخارة الله ، ومن سعادة ابن آدم رضاه بما قضى الله ، ومن شقاوة ابن آدم تركه استخارة الله ، ومن شقاوة ابن آدم سخطه بما قضى الله . وثانيها : ما روى عبد الله بن عمر : أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يقول: «اللهم إني أسألك الصحة والعفة والأمانة وحسن الخلق والرضاء بالقدر » وثالثها : ما روى عبد الله بن شداد قال : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : « اللهم رضني بقضائك ، وبارك لي في قدرك ، حتى لا أحب تأخير ما عجلت ولا تعجيل ما أخرت » ورابعها : إن من مشاهير الأخبار الربانية : أنه : حكى عن رب العزة أنه يقول : « ومن لم يرض بقضائي ، فليطلب رباً سواي ) . وأما الآثار فكثيرة : أحدها : قال أبو الدرداء : « المروءة أربع خلال : الصبر للحكم ، والرضاء بالقدر ، والإخلاص في التوكل ، والاستسلام للموت ، وعنه أيضاً أنه قال : « إن الله إذا قضى قضاء ، أحب أن يرضى بقضائه ، وثانيها : عن عمران بن حصين أنه قال : ثلاث يدرك بهن العبد رغائب الدنيا والآخرة : الصبر عند البلاء ، والرضا بالقدر ، والدعاء في الرخاء ، وثالثها : روى محمد بن كعب : أن موسى عليه السلام قال : « أي ربي أي خلقك أعظم ذنباً ؟ ، قال : « الذي يتهمني ، قال : « أي ربي ، وهل يتهمك أحد ؟ ، قال : ( نعم الذي يستخيرني ولا يرضى بقضائي ، ورابعها : قيل فيها أوحي الله تعالى إلى داود عليه السلام : « يا داود إنك لن تلقاني بعمل هو أرضى لي عنك ، ولا أحط لوزرك من الرضا بقضائي ) . فثبت بهذه الوجوه : أنه لو كان الكفر بقضاء الله لكان الرضا به واجباً وأما بيان أنه لا يجوز الرضا بالكفر والعصيان : فهذا أيضاً مجمع عليه بين الأمة . ثم الدليل عليه : القرآن والخبر . أما القرآن : فهو أن الظالم يجب لعنه . لقوله تعالى : ( ألا لعنة الله على الظالمين ) وذلك ينافي وجوب الرضا بظلمه . وأيضاً : فالأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر واجب بأقصى الوجوه . وذلك يمنع من وجوب حصول الرضا بالكفر والفسق
Know: that whatever reports have come, of command and prohibition, praise and blame, reward and punishment, encouragement and discouragement, the people argue with them. And its explanation is according to the way mentioned in the Quranic proofs. Then after this they adhere to other aspects: The first proof: If disbelief and wickedness occurred by the creation of God Almighty and His decree, then being pleased with them would be obligatory. But being pleased with them is not permissible, so it must be that they are not by the creation of God nor by His decree. Explanation of the entailment: Everything that is by the decree of God, then being pleased with it is obligatory, for that is agreed upon by the community. Then we say: The proof of it also is the Quran, the report, and the tradition. As for the Quran: His saying Almighty (And it is not for a believing man or a believing woman, when God and His Messenger have decreed a matter, that they should have any choice in their matter). As for reports, many: One of them: what Sa'd ibn Malik narrated, said: the Messenger of God said: 'Among the happiness of the son of Adam is his seeking guidance from God, and among the happiness of the son of Adam is his being pleased with what God decrees, and among the misery of the son of Adam is his abandoning seeking guidance from God, and among the misery of the son of Adam is his displeasure with what God decrees.' Second: what Abdullah ibn Umar narrated: that the Messenger of God used to say: 'O God, I ask You for health, chastity, trustworthiness, good character, and being pleased with destiny.' Third: what Abdullah ibn Shaddad narrated, said: the Messenger of God used to say: 'O God, make me pleased with Your decree, and bless me in Your destiny, so that I do not love delay of what You have hastened nor hastening of what You have delayed.' Fourth: among the famous divine reports: that it is narrated from the Lord of Might that He says: 'Whoever is not pleased with My decree, let him seek a lord other than Me.' As for traditions, many: One of them: Abu Darda said: 'Manliness consists of four traits: patience under judgement, being pleased with destiny, sincerity in trust, and surrender to death.' And also from him: 'When God decrees a decree, He loves that one be pleased with His decree.' Second: from Imran ibn Husain: 'Three things by which the servant attains the desires of this world and the Hereafter: patience at calamity, being pleased with destiny, and supplication in prosperity.' Third: Muhammad ibn Kab narrated that Moses said: 'O my Lord, which of Your creation is greatest in sin?' He said: 'The one who accuses Me.' He said: 'O my Lord, does anyone accuse You?' He said: 'Yes, the one who seeks guidance from Me and is not pleased with My decree.' Fourth: it is said in revelation to David: 'O David, you will not meet Me with a deed more pleasing to Me from you, nor more lightening of your burden, than being pleased with My decree.' So it is established by these aspects that if disbelief were by the decree of God, then being pleased with it would be obligatory. As for the explanation that being pleased with disbelief and disobedience is not permissible: this also is agreed upon by the community. Then the proof of it is the Quran and the report. As for the Quran: that the wrongdoer must be cursed, because of His saying Almighty: (Beware, the curse of God is upon the wrongdoers). And that contradicts the obligation of being pleased with his wrongdoing. Also: commanding good and forbidding evil is obligatory in the strongest manner. And that prevents the obligation of obtaining being pleased with disbelief and wickedness.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage presents the first proof (al-hujjah al-ula) used by a group referred to as 'al-qawm' (the people) — likely the Qadariyya or Mu'tazila who deny that God creates human actions, particularly evil ones. They argue that if disbelief (kufr) and wickedness (fisq) were created by God and decreed by Him, then being pleased (rida) with them would be obligatory. However, being pleased with them is not permissible (la yajuz), so they cannot be from God's creation or decree. The argument is structured as an entailment (mulazama): they first prove the major premise — that everything from God's decree requires being pleased with it. They claim this is agreed upon (mujma' 'alayh) by the community. Then they support this premise with evidence from the Quran, reports (akhbar), and traditions (athar). They cite Quran 33:36, several hadith about the virtue of being pleased with God's decree, and sayings of the salaf (e.g., Abu Darda, Imran ibn Husain) and prophetic traditions emphasizing contentment with divine decree. After establishing the major premise, they affirm the minor premise: that being pleased with disbelief and disobedience is not permissible. This too is claimed to be agreed upon, and they support it with Quranic evidence that wrongdoers are cursed (Quran 7:44) and the obligation of commanding good and forbidding evil, which precludes being pleased with evil. The overall argument is a classic Qadariyya proof that since God's decree demands acceptance, and evil cannot be accepted, evil cannot be from God's decree. The text presents the argument without immediate refutation here.

Key Terms
قضاء
رضا
الملازمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT cited as evidence for the obligation to be pleased with divine decree?
A) Quran 33:36
B) Hadith: 'From the happiness of the son of Adam is his being pleased with what God decrees'
C) Athar from Ibn Abbas about the virtue of patience
D) Story of Musa being told that accusing God is the greatest sin

Key Takeaway
The Qadariyya build a strong case from Quran, hadith, and early tradition that being pleased with Allah's decree is an obligation, not merely recommended.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a recent disappointment or trial. When you inwardly disliked what happened, did you realize that such displeasure is a form of accusing Allah? How will you train your heart to embrace rida starting today?
?
The hadith says displeasure with decree is a cause of misery. Is there any ongoing misery in your life rooted in your refusal to accept Allah's choice? What concrete step will you take this week to surrender to His qada'?
?
The Prophet prayed, 'O Allah, make me pleased with Your decree.' When was the last time you made this dua with full presence of heart? Will you commit to reciting it daily for the next seven days, and reflect on what changes it brings?

Divine Decree
intermediate
6 min
The Minor Premise: Rida with Kufr is Impermissible
Qadariyya proof that rida with disbelief is forbidden, completing their argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Qadariyya's argument that being pleased with kufr and disobedience is not permissible, completing their proof that kufr cannot be from divine decree.

Core Idea
Since wrongdoers are cursed and commanding good is obligatory, being pleased with evil is forbidden.

Having established the general rule that everything from Allah's decree requires rida, the Qadariyya now turn to the minor premise: that being pleased with kufr and fisq is not permissible. They claim this too is agreed upon, and they support it with Quranic verses about cursing wrongdoers and the obligation of enjoining good and forbidding evil. This completes their argument against divine decree of kufr.

Guided Path
1
Read the final portion
Read the Arabic and translation from 'fa-thabata bi-hadhihi al-wujuh' to the end.
This concludes the first proof.
2
Understand the minor premise
Identify the claim: being pleased with kufr and disobedience is not permissible (la yajuz). Note that this is also claimed to be consensus.
3
Examine the first piece of evidence
The Qadariyya cite Quran 7:44 which curses wrongdoers. Explain how cursing contradicts being pleased.
4
Examine the second piece of evidence
The obligation of commanding good and forbidding evil is invoked. Why does this prevent rida with evil?
If we must forbid evil, we cannot be inwardly pleased with it.
5
Synthesize the full argument
Combine the major premise (rida with decree is wajib) and minor premise (rida with kufr is impermissible) to reach the conclusion that kufr is not from decree.
This is the logical conclusion of the first proof.

Key Terms

الفسق
الظالمون
الأمر بالمعروف
النهي عن المنكر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that being pleased with whatever happens includes being pleased with sin, so we should not be upset by evil.
Correction: Islamic teaching distinguishes between accepting divine decree as from Allah (i.e., acknowledging that it could only happen by His will) and being pleased with the moral evil itself. We must hate evil but accept the decree.

Checkpoint
Which Quranic verse does the Qadariyya use to support the impermissibility of being pleased with wrongdoing?
A) 'Allah does not love corruption' (2:205)
B) 'Beware, the curse of Allah is upon the wrongdoers' (7:44)
C) 'And those who believe and do righteous deeds...' (5:9)
D) 'O you who believe, take not the Jews and Christians as allies' (5:51)

Key Takeaway
The Qadariyya's first proof argues that because rida with kufr is forbidden, kufr cannot originate from Allah's decree, which would otherwise demand rida.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a sin being committed—whether in society or in your own heart—are you truly displeased with it as Allah is? Or do you sometimes feel a secret approval, excusing it as 'part of life'? This passage demands that you search your soul: Do your emotions align with Allah's curse on wrongdoers, or have you made peace with things He has cursed? What will you do today to cultivate genuine hatred for evil, starting with the sins you have normalized?
?
The obligation to enjoin good and forbid evil is described here as 'obligatory in the strongest manner'. Yet how often do you remain silent when you see something wrong, perhaps to avoid conflict or discomfort? If you truly believe that rida with kufr is impermissible, then your silence is a form of approval. Which specific situation in your life—at home, work, or among friends—is calling you to speak up, and what is holding you back from fulfilling this duty?
?
If someone were to examine your life—your entertainment choices, your reactions to injustice, your inner thoughts—would they find that you are pleased with things Allah has cursed? This passage confronts you with the fact that approval of sin is itself a sin. What hidden pleasures or attitudes do you need to repent of so that your heart is no longer at ease with what Allah hates?

The Obligation of Rida with God's Decree
The author compiles multiple hadiths and traditions emphasizing rida with God's decree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Islamic texts strongly emphasize the virtue and even obligation of being pleased with God's decree (rida bi'l-qada'), providing the foundation for the argument about kufr.

Core Idea
Being pleased with God's decree is a prophetic and divine command.

In this lesson, we examine the extensive textual evidence the author presents to demonstrate that rida (satisfaction) with God's decree is a central virtue and even an obligation. These include hadiths of the Prophet, divine sayings, and statements of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadiths and traditions
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the translation. Notice that the author lists several reports from the Prophet and early Muslims.
Pay attention to the variety of sources: prophetic supplications, divine speech, and statements of Companions.
2
Identify the common theme
Each report emphasizes the importance of being satisfied with God's decree or destiny. List the key phrases that express this theme.
3
Understand the logical implication
The author concludes from these reports that if kufr (disbelief) were by God's decree, then being satisfied with it would be obligatory. This is a conditional statement that sets up the next part of the proof.
This conclusion is drawn directly from the collected evidence.
4
Prepare for the next lesson
Consider what would happen if rida with kufr is not obligatory. The next lesson will examine the prohibition of rida with kufr and complete the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بما قضى الله . وثانيها : ما روى عبد الله بن عمر : أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يقول: «اللهم إني أسألك الصحة والعفة والأمانة وحسن الخلق والرضاء بالقدر » وثالثها : ما روى عبد الله بن شداد قال : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : اللهم رضني بقضائك ، وبارك لي في قدرك ، حتى لا أحب تأخير ما عجلت ولا تعجيل ما أخرت ورابعها : إن من مشاهير الأخبار الربانية : أنه حكى عن رب العزة أنه يقول : « ومن لم يرض بقضائي ، فليطلب ربا سواي ) . وأما الآثار فكثيرة : أحدها : قال أبو الدرداء : « المروءة أربع خلال : الصبر للحكم ، والرضاء بالقدر ، والإخلاص في التوكل ، والاستسلام للموت ، وعنه أيضاً أنه قال : « إن الله إذا قضى قضاء ، أحب أن يرضى بقضائه ، وثانيها : عن عمران بن حصين أنه قال : ثلاث يدرك بهن العبد رغائب الدنيا والآخرة : الصبر عند البلاء ، والرضا بالقدر ، والدعاء في الرخاء ، وثالثها : روى محمد بن كعب : أن موسى عليه السلام قال : أي ربي أي خلقك أعظم ذنباً ؟ ، قال : « الذي يتهمني ، قال : « أي ربي ، وهل يتهمك أحد ؟ ، قال : ( نعم الذي يستخيرني ولا يرضى بقضائي ، ورابعها : قيل فيها أوحي الله تعالى إلى داود عليه السلام : « يا داود إنك لن تلقاني بعمل هو أرضى لي عنك ، ولا أحط لوزرك من الرضا بقضائي ) . فثبت بهذه الوجوه : أنه لو كان الكفر بقضاء الله لكان الرضا به واجباً . وأما بيان أنه لا يجوز الرضا بالكفر والعصيان : فهذا أيضاً مجمع عليه بين الأمة . ثم الدليل عليه : القرآن والخبر . أما القرآن : فهو أن الظالم يجب لعنه . لقوله تعالى : ( ألا لعنة الله على الظالمين ) وذلك ينافي وجوب الرضا بظلمه . وأيضاً : فالأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر واجب بأقصى الوجوه . وذلك يمنع من وجوب حصول الرضا بالكفر والفسق . وأما الخبر : فما روى أنه قال : ( الرضا بالكفر : كفر ) فثبت : أنه لو كان الكفر بقضاء الله ، لكان الرضا به واجباً ، وثبت : أن الرضا به غير واجب ، فوجب أن لا يكون الكفر واقعاً بقضاء الله ولا بخلقه . وهو المطلوب .
With what God decreed. Second: what 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar reported: that the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) used to say: 'O God, I ask You for health, chastity, trustworthiness, good character, and satisfaction with destiny (al-rida bi'l-qadar).' Third: what 'Abdullah ibn Shaddad reported: he said: the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) used to say: 'O God, make me satisfied with Your decree (qada'), and bless me in Your destiny (qadar), so that I do not love to delay what You have hastened nor hasten what You have delayed.' Fourth: it is among the famous divine reports that it is related from the Lord of Might that He says: 'Whoever is not satisfied with My decree, let him seek a Lord other than Me.' As for the traditions (athar), they are many: First: Abu al-Darda' said: 'Manliness consists of four traits: patience in judgment, satisfaction with destiny, sincerity in trust, and submission to death.' And also from him that he said: 'When God decrees a decree, He loves that one be satisfied with His decree.' Second: from 'Imran ibn Husayn that he said: 'Three things by which the servant obtains the desires of this world and the Hereafter: patience at the time of trial, satisfaction with destiny, and supplication in times of ease.' Third: Muhammad ibn Ka'b reported that Moses (peace be upon him) said: 'My Lord, which of Your creatures is greatest in sin?' He said: 'The one who accuses Me.' He said: 'My Lord, does anyone accuse You?' He said: 'Yes, the one who seeks my guidance (istikharah) and is not satisfied with My decree.' Fourth: it is said that God revealed to David (peace be upon him): 'O David, you will never meet Me with a deed more pleasing to Me from you, nor more reducing of your burden, than satisfaction with My decree.' So it is established by these proofs: that if disbelief (kufr) were by the decree of God, then being satisfied with it would be obligatory. As for the demonstration that it is not permissible to be satisfied with disbelief and disobedience, this too is a matter of consensus among the community. Then the proof for it is the Qur'an and the hadith. As for the Qur'an: the wrongdoer must be cursed, due to His saying: 'Surely the curse of God is upon the wrongdoers.' That contradicts the obligation of being satisfied with his wrongdoing. Also, commanding good and forbidding evil is obligatory in the strongest sense, and that prevents the obligation of attaining satisfaction with disbelief and sin. As for the hadith: it is reported that he said: 'Satisfaction with disbelief is disbelief.' So it is established that if disbelief were by the decree of God, then being satisfied with it would be obligatory, and it is established that being satisfied with it is not obligatory. Therefore, it is necessary that disbelief does not occur by the decree of God nor by His creation. That is the desired conclusion.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage presents a proof by contradiction. The author first compiles multiple hadiths and traditions emphasizing the virtue and even obligation of being pleased (rida) with God's decree (qada') and destiny (qadar). The evidence includes prophetic supplications, divine statements, and sayings of the Companions. The conclusion from these is that if disbelief (kufr) were by God's decree, then being pleased with it would be obligatory. Then the author demonstrates that being pleased with disbelief is not obligatory; rather, it is forbidden. He supports this with Qur'anic verses that command cursing wrongdoers and commanding good while forbidding evil, and with the hadith 'Satisfaction with disbelief is disbelief.' Since the obligation of rida with kufr (if it were decreed) contradicts the clear prohibition of rida with kufr, the premise that kufr is decreed by God is false. Thus, kufr is not by God's decree nor is it His creation.

Key Terms
الرضا بالقضاء
القضاء
القدر

A) Patience at the time of trial
B) Satisfaction with destiny
C) Supplication in times of ease
D) Generosity to the poor

Key Takeaway
The Islamic tradition strongly emphasizes the virtue and obligation of being pleased with God's decree.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When a long-held hope of yours collapses—a marriage, a career, a dream—what rises in your heart: rida or resentment? Be honest. If resentment, what would it cost you to stop seeking another lord and surrender to Him who decreed it?
?
Do you truly believe that God's decree is better for you than your own choices? If so, why do you still delay accepting outcomes you dislike? What would it mean for your dua tonight if you meant 'Your will be done' with your whole chest?
?
The Prophet asked to be made satisfied so that he would not love to delay what God hastened. Where in your life are you secretly wishing God had waited—or acted sooner—and thus questioning His wisdom?

The Prohibition of Rida with Kufr and Conclusion
The author presents scriptural proofs against rida with kufr and concludes the argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why rida with kufr is forbidden and how this leads to the conclusion that kufr is not decreed by God.

Core Idea
Rida with kufr is forbidden, so kufr cannot be decreed.

After establishing that rida with God's decree is obligatory, the author now demonstrates the other side: rida with kufr is prohibited by consensus, Qur'an, and hadith. This contradiction proves that kufr is not decreed.

Guided Path
1
Read the Qur'anic and hadith evidence
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. The author presents proof from the Qur'an (cursing wrongdoers, commanding good) and a hadith ('Rida with kufr is kufr').
2
Understand the logical structure
The argument is a proof by contradiction: if kufr were decreed, rida with it would be wajib (from previous lesson). But rida with kufr is forbidden, so kufr cannot be decreed.
This is the core of the whole proof.
3
Grasp the final conclusion
The author concludes that kufr does not occur by God's decree nor is it created by Him. This is the desired result (al-matlub).

Second Proof: God's Dislike Entails Non-Creation
The author uses hadith to argue that disliked things are not willed, hence not created.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses the principle that a thing cannot be both disliked and intended under the same aspect to prove that what God dislikes is not created by Him.

Core Idea
What God dislikes, He does not will; what He does not will, He does not create.

In this passage, the author presents a second proof against the idea that God creates evil or disliked things. He cites a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) lists three things God dislikes. The author then applies a logical principle: one thing under one aspect cannot be both disliked and intended by God simultaneously. Since creation is tied to God's will, anything He dislikes cannot be willed and therefore cannot be created by Him. A similar proof is offered from another hadith about divorce.

Guided Path
1
Understand the hadith evidence
The author begins by quoting a hadith: 'God has disliked for you three things: idle talk, excessive questioning, and wasting wealth.' Recognize that these are actions that God dislikes.
2
Apply the logical principle
The author states that a single thing under one aspect cannot be both disliked and intended at the same time. Since God dislikes these things, they cannot be intended (willed) by Him. Reflect on why this logical principle is crucial.
3
Connect to creation
The author concludes that if something is not willed by God, it cannot be created, because creation only occurs through will. Then consider the second hadith about divorce as further evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية : قوله : ( إن الله كره لكم ثلاث : قيل وقال وكثرة السؤال وإضاعة المال ، ولما كانت هذه الأشياء الثلاثة مكروهة الله تعالى ، وجب أن لا تكون مرادة له . لأن الشيء الواحد بالاعتبار الواحد لا يكون مكروهاً ومرادا معاً . وإذا لم يكن مراداً الله تعالى ، وجب أن لا يكون مخلوقاً له ، لأن الخلق لا يحصل إلا بالإرادة . ويقرب منه الاستدلال بقوله : أبغض المباحات إلى الله الطلاق ، دل النص على أن الطلاق مبغوض الله ، والمبغوض لا يكون مراداً وما لا يكون مراداً الله لا يكون مخلوقاً له
The second proof: His statement: 'Indeed, God has disliked for you three things: idle talk, excessive questioning, and wasting wealth.' Since these three things are disliked by God, it is necessary that they are not intended (murada) by Him, because one thing under one aspect cannot be both disliked and intended simultaneously. And if they are not intended by God, it is necessary that they are not created by Him, because creation does not occur except through will (irada). Close to this is the proof by His statement: 'The most hateful of permissible things to God is divorce.' The text indicates that divorce is hated by God, and what is hated is not intended, and what is not intended by God is not created by Him.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage presents a proof based on a hadith where God states He dislikes three things: idle talk, excessive questioning, and wasting wealth. The author reasons that since these are disliked (makruha), they cannot be intended (murada) by God, because a single thing cannot simultaneously be both disliked and intended under the same aspect. Since creation (khalq) only occurs through God's will (irada), if something is not willed, it cannot be created. The author then offers a similar proof from another hadith: 'The most hateful of permissible things to God is divorce.' The same logic applies: what God hates (mabghud) is not willed, and what is not willed is not created.

Key Terms
الكراهية
الإرادة
الخلق
المبغوض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God can create things He dislikes even if He does not will them.
Correction: Creation only occurs through God's will, and if He dislikes something, it cannot be willed under that aspect, so it cannot be created by Him.

Checkpoint
What logical principle does the author use in this proof?
A) One thing cannot be both disliked and intended under the same aspect.
B) God cannot create what He dislikes because of His perfection.
C) Creation requires power, not will.
D) Dislike implies imperfection in God.

Key Takeaway
God's dislike of something logically entails that He does not will it, and therefore does not create it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God dislikes idle talk, why do you still engage in it? What does your willingness to do what He dislikes say about your heart's alignment with His will? Will you commit today to avoid one form of idle talk?
?
You may have experienced or witnessed divorce—a thing God hates. How does knowing that God does not will or create such hated things change the way you view that trial? Can you trust that God's will for you is entirely good, even when you face what He hates?
?
This lesson argues that what God dislikes cannot be willed or created by Him. Consider a sin you struggle with. Do you believe God wills that sin to happen? If not, then how do you explain its existence, and what responsibility do you have to align your choices with what God wills and loves?

Third Proof: Seeking Refuge from Satan Shows His Acts Are Not from God
The author uses a hadith to argue against the Jabariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a hadith about seeking refuge from Satan leads to a reductio ad absurdum argument against the Jabariyya claim that all actions are created by God.

Core Idea
If Satan's actions were from God, we would seek refuge from God, not Satan.

This lesson presents a powerful logical proof grounded in a prophetic hadith. The Prophet taught us to say 'O God, protect me from Satan' when leaving the mosque. But if Satan's actions were created by God, as the Jabariyya claim, then we would essentially be asking God to protect us from Himself—an absurdity. This argument shows that not all actions can be attributed to God's direct creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith text
Begin by reading the Arabic hadith and its translation. Note the specific supplications mentioned for entering and leaving the mosque.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Hurayrah.
2
Understand the logical argument
The author draws a reductio ad absurdum: if Satan's actions were created by God, then the supplication 'protect me from Satan' would effectively mean 'protect me from You.' This is absurd and was never taught by the Prophet.
This shows that the Jabariyya position leads to an inconsistency with Islamic practice.
3
Apply the reasoning to other supplications
The same reasoning applies to all similar du'as, such as 'I seek refuge in You from the evil of everything You seize by the forelock.' The argument refutes the Jabariyya claim that all evils come from God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة : ما روى أبو هريرة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : « إذا دخل أحدكم المسجد فليسلم على النبي . ثم ليقل : ( اللهم افتح لي أبواب رحمتك ، وإذا خرج فليسلم ، وليقل : ( اللهم أجرني من الشيطان ، ولو كان فعل الشيطان قد حصل بإيجاد الله تعالى ، لوجب أن يقول : اللهم أجرني منك . وهكذا القول في سائر الأدعية . كقوله : ( أعوذ بك من شر كل شيء ، أنت آخذ بناصيته » لأن كل الشرور من الله تعالى على قول المجبرة .
The third proof: What Abu Hurayrah reported: that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When one of you enters the mosque, let him greet the Prophet, then let him say: "O God, open for me the doors of Your mercy." And when he leaves, let him greet, and let him say: "O God, protect me from Satan."' If the action of Satan had occurred by the creation (ijad) of God, then it would be necessary for him to say: 'O God, protect me from You.' The same applies to all other supplications, such as his saying: 'I seek refuge in You from the evil of everything You seize by the forelock,' because all evils are from God according to the Jabariyya.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage presents a reductio ad absurdum argument. The author cites a hadith where the Prophet teaches to say 'O God, protect me from Satan' when leaving the mosque. If Satan's actions were created (ijad) by God, then logically one should say 'O God, protect me from You,' since the source of harm would be God. But no one says this, and the Prophet did not teach it. The same reasoning applies to all similar supplications, such as 'I seek refuge in You from the evil of everything You seize by the forelock.' The author notes that the Jabariyya (fatalists) believe all evils come from God, but this hadith shows that cannot be true, because supplication would be directed to God against Himself, which is absurd.

Key Terms
الاستعاذة
الشيطان
الإيجاد
المجبرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Jabariyya claim that all actions, including those of Satan, are created by God.
Correction: This proof shows that if that were true, seeking refuge from Satan would be meaningless, as it would be seeking refuge from God Himself.

Checkpoint
What absurd consequence would follow if Satan's actions were created by God?
A) One would have to seek refuge from God Himself.
B) Satan would be blameless.
C) God would be unjust.
D) The Prophet would not have taught the du'a.

Key Takeaway
The hadith about seeking refuge from Satan logically refutes the Jabariyya claim that all actions are from God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'A'udhu billahi minash shaytanir rajim', do you sincerely believe that Shaytan's actions are not directly from Allah? How does that belief shape your sense of personal responsibility to resist him, knowing that Allah has given you the means to seek refuge?
?
If you were to adopt the fatalistic view that every evil act comes from Allah, how would your duas change? Would you stop asking for protection from Shaytan? Examine your heart: are there moments when you subconsciously blame Allah for your own failures to resist sin?
?
The Prophet taught specific duas for entering and leaving the mosque. Do you practice them with the understanding that they reflect a deeper theological truth about the source of good and evil? What would it cost you to neglect these duas and the lesson they carry about divine justice and human accountability?

God's Patience as Dislike: Proof He Does Not Create Evil Speech
Interpretation of a hadith to prove God's non-creation of evil speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a hadith about God's patience is interpreted as intense dislike, leading to the conclusion that God does not create evil speech.

Core Idea
God's patience means intense dislike, not approval.

This lesson examines a hadith in which God is described as most patient with harm. The author argues that this patience actually signifies God's intense hatred of the polytheists' statements. From this, we deduce that God cannot be the creator of such speech, because He does not will it and is neither compelled nor forgetful.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and the argument
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the hadith and how the author interprets God's 'patience' as intense dislike.
2
Understand the reinterpretation of 'patience'
The author redefines 'patience' as 'shiddat al-karahiyya' (intense dislike). Ask yourself why this is a key move.
This avoids the problematic idea that God passively endorses evil.
3
Trace the logical inference
Follow the reasoning: intense dislike implies God does not will the speech. Since He is not compelled or forgetful, if He does not will it, He does not do it. Therefore, He does not create it.
This uses the principle that will (irada) is necessary for action in a non-compelled agent.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The conclusion is that God does not create evil speech (e.g., attributing partners to Him). Consider how this supports the Ash'ari position on human free will and divine creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة : روى سعيد بن جبير عن أبي عبد الرحمن السلمي ، عن عبد الله بن قيس عن النبي أنه قال : « ما أحد أصبر على أذي سمعه ، من الله ، يجعلون له نداً ، ويجعلون له ولداً ، وهو يرزقهم ويعافيهم ويعطيهم ، وجه الاستدلال به: إن المراد من هذا الصبر شدة كراهية الله تعالى لهذا الكلام. وذلك يدل على أنه تعالى يكرهه ، وإذا كان كذلك ، وجب أن لا يكون الله خالقاً له ، لأن من لم يكن ملجأ للفعل ولا ساهياً ، فإنه إذا كان لا يريده لم يفعله
The fourth proof: Sa'id ibn Jubayr reported from Abu 'Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami, from 'Abdullah ibn Qays, from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'No one is more patient with harm that he hears than God. They attribute to Him a rival, and they attribute to Him a son, while He provides for them, gives them health, and gives them.' The aspect of the proof is: that what is meant by this patience is the intensity of God's dislike (karahiyya) for this speech. That indicates that He dislikes it. If this is the case, then it is necessary that God is not its creator, because whoever is not compelled (mulja') to do an action nor forgetful (sahi), if He does not will it, He does not do it.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage presents a proof from a hadith describing God's patience with those who attribute partners and children to Him. The author interprets 'patience' (sabr) not as passive endurance but as intense dislike (shiddat al-karahiyya). Therefore, God intensely dislikes such speech. Since He dislikes it and is neither compelled (mulja') nor forgetful (sahi), if He does not will (irada) a thing, He does not do it. Hence, He does not create that speech. The reasoning is that God's non-creation follows from His not willing it, which follows from His disliking it.

Key Terms
الصبر
الكراهية
الخلق
الملجأ
الساهي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's 'patience' (sabr) with evil speech means He is indifferent or approves of it.
Correction: The author clarifies that 'patience' here means intense dislike (shiddat al-karahiyya), not passive acceptance.

Checkpoint
How does the author interpret God's 'patience' (sabr) in the hadith?
A) As weakness or inability to act.
B) As intense dislike (karahiyya shadida).
C) As indifference to the harm.
D) As approval of the polytheists' statements.

Key Takeaway
God's 'patience' in the hadith is understood as intense dislike, which leads to the conclusion that He does not create the evil speech He dislikes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you speak ill of others or engage in backbiting, do you presume that God's patience with your speech means He tolerates it? After learning that God's patience is actually intense dislike, how does that change your attitude towards your own idle words? Will you commit to seeking forgiveness for your speech today?
?
The hadith mentions that despite people attributing rivals and children to God, He still provides for them. Are there areas in your life where you test God's patience by persisting in sinful habits, assuming He will 'put up with it'? How will you respond to the fact that God's patience is not passive acceptance but active displeasure?
?
The proof concludes that God does not create evil speech because He dislikes it and does not will it. If you find yourself using language that is harmful or disrespectful to others, consider: are you, by your own free will, creating speech that God dislikes? What will you do today to align your speech with what God wills?

The Ninth Proof: Hadith of the Workers in the Vineyard
Ninth proof using a hadith to show actions are not created by Allah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a prophetic hadith about different communities' rewards demonstrates that human actions are not created by Allah but are our own acquisition.

Core Idea
Reward for actions proves actions are ours, not Allah's direct creation.

This lesson presents the ninth proof from the text, which uses a well-known hadith to refute the view that all actions are directly created by Allah. The hadith compares the work of the people of the Torah, Gospel, and Qur'an, showing that reward is given based on effort and action. From this, the author argues that reward cannot be for what Allah creates in us (like colors or forms), so our actions must be our own.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and translation
Read the Arabic hadith once, then its literal translation. Notice the story of the three communities receiving different rewards for their work.
The hadith is a parable about work and reward.
2
Identify the key elements of the story
Look at the different work periods (from afternoon prayer to sunset, etc.) and the resulting rewards (one qirat vs. two qirats). Note the complaint of the earlier communities and Allah's response.
The response 'This is My favor; I give it to whom I will' is crucial.
3
Understand the point of evidence (وجه الاستدلال)
The author states that reward cannot be deserved for what Allah creates directly in us (like our physical attributes). Since reward is mentioned, the actions that earned the reward must be our own, not Allah's creation.
This is a logical inference: if reward is for actions, and reward is not for created things, then actions are not created by Allah.
4
Reflect on the theological conclusion
The proof refutes the Jabriyya who claim all actions are created by Allah. If that were true, then reward would be meaningless or unjust. Therefore, actions are acquired by humans.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة التاسعة : روى أبو عمر قال : سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول وهو قائم على المنبر : « إنما بقاؤكم فيمن سلف قبلكم كما بين صلاة العصر إلى غروب الشمس ، أعطي أهل التوراة التوراة ، فعملوا بها حتى إذا انتصف النهار عجزوا عنها . فأعطوا قيراطاً قيراطاً . وأعطي أهل الإنجيل الإنجيل فعملوا به ، حتى إذا بلغوا صلاة العصر ، عجزوا . فأعطوا قيراطاً قيراطاً . وأعطيتم القرآن فعملتم به ، حتى إذا غربت الشمس أعطيتم قيراطين قيراطين . قال أهل التوراة والإنجيل : ربنا هؤلاء أقل عملاً وأكثر جزاء . فقال الله : هل ظلمتكم من أجركم شيئاً؟ فقالوا : لا . فقال : فضلي أوتيه من أشاء . ووجه الاستدلال به : أنه لا يصح استحقاق الأجر والثواب على ما يخلقه الله فينا كألواننا وصورنا ، وحيث أثبت الله الأجر ظهر أن أفعالنا ليست بخلق الله
The ninth proof: Abu 'Umar narrated: I heard the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, say while standing on the pulpit: 'Your remaining compared to those before you is like between the afternoon prayer and sunset. The people of the Torah were given the Torah and acted upon it until midday when they became unable. So they were given a qirat each. The people of the Gospel were given the Gospel and acted upon it until the afternoon prayer when they became unable. So they were given a qirat each. And you were given the Qur'an and acted upon it until sunset, so you were given two qirats each. The people of the Torah and Gospel said: Our Lord, these did less work and got more reward. Allah said: Have I wronged you in your wages? They said: No. He said: This is My favor; I give it to whom I will.' The point of evidence from it: It is not valid to deserve reward and recompense for what Allah creates in us, like our colors and forms. And since Allah established the reward, it becomes clear that our actions are not created by Allah.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage presents the ninth proof, which is a hadith from the Prophet about the different communities receiving different rewards based on their actions. The point of evidence is that reward is given for actions that are performed by the individuals, not for things that Allah creates directly in them, such as colors or forms. If rewards were for creations of Allah, then everyone would deserve reward equally regardless of effort. Since reward is differentiated based on action, it shows that actions are not created by Allah but are the acts of the servants.

Key Terms
القيراط
الأجر
الاستدلال
خلق الأفعال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that reward is purely from Allah's favor and not based on human action, or that all actions are created by Allah so humans have no real role.
Correction: The hadith shows that reward is tied to action and effort. The author explains that reward cannot be for what Allah creates directly in us, so actions must be our own. Thus, actions are not created by Allah but are acquired by humans.

Checkpoint

A) The Qur'an community got the most reward because they worked longest.
B) Reward cannot be for things Allah creates in us, so actions must be ours.
C) The people of the Torah and Gospel complained about injustice.
D) Allah's favor is arbitrary.

Key Takeaway
Actions are our own because reward is based on them, not on Allah's direct creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The earlier communities complained about Allah's distribution of favor. Have you ever felt resentment that others seem to receive more reward with less effort? What does that reveal about your understanding of Allah's justice and mercy? How will you combat that feeling when it arises?
?
If your actions are truly your own and will be rewarded accordingly, what is one habit or sin you have been excusing as 'outside your control'? Will you own it today and repent with a firm resolve to change?

The Tenth Proof: Intention is Better than Action
Tenth proof citing the hadith to affirm human action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith 'The intention of a person is better than his action' is used as a proof that actions belong to human beings and not to Allah.

Core Idea
A hadith attributing action to a person proves human free will.

The tenth proof in this series is remarkably concise, using a single prophetic hadith to affirm that actions are attributable to the servant. This short but powerful argument draws on the linguistic implication of the statement. Let's examine how the author uses this hadith to make his point.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the simplicity of the argument: a hadith followed by a direct conclusion.
The hadith is well-known; focus on how it is used as evidence.
2
Identify the key phrase
Focus on the phrase 'وهذا تصريح بإثبات العمل للعبد' which is the author's conclusion. Understand what 'تصريح' (explicit affirmation) means here.
The author claims the hadith explicitly affirms action to the servant.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why attributing action to the servant is significant for the qadar debate. If the action belongs to the servant, it cannot be solely created by Allah.
This counters the view that all actions are directly from Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة العاشرة : قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : « نية المرء خير من عمله » وهذا تصريح بإثبات العمل للعبد
The tenth proof: His saying, peace be upon him: 'The intention of a person is better than his action.' And this is an explicit affirmation of the action belonging to the servant.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This is a very short proof. The author cites the hadith 'The intention of a person is better than his action.' The point is that the action is attributed to the person (العبد), not to Allah. This is used as evidence that actions are created by the servant, not by Allah.

The Sacred Hadith on Divine Justice
The hadith qudsi cited by Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the content and structure of the hadith qudsi that the Mu'tazila use as evidence for their doctrine of free will.

Core Idea
The hadith emphasizes human accountability and God's self-forbiddance of injustice.

This sacred hadith, narrated by the Prophet, presents God's direct address to humanity. It highlights God's mercy, provision, and the principle that each person is responsible for their own deeds. The Mu'tazila later build their arguments on specific phrases from this hadith.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic hadith carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to familiarize yourself with the sacred text. Notice the repetition of 'يا عبادي' (O My servants).
The hadith is a direct divine address.
2
Identify key themes
Look for themes: God's self-forbiddance of injustice, forgiveness, provision, and the conclusion about deeds belonging to the servants.
3
Focus on the concluding statement
Pay special attention to the last part: 'These are your deeds... whoever finds good, praise God; whoever finds other, blame no one but himself.' This is central to the Mu'tazilite position.
This statement directly attributes actions to humans.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلا تظالموا . يا عبادي إنكم الذين تخطئون بالليل والنهار وأنا أغفر الذنوب جميعاً ، ولا أبالي . فاستغفروني أغفر لكم . يا عبادي كلكم جائع إلا أطعمته فاستطعموني أطعمكم . يا عبادي كلكم عاري إلا من كسوته فاستكسوني أكسكم يا عبادي لو أن أولكم وآخركم وإنسكم وجنكم كانوا على أتقى قلب رجل واحد لم يزد ذلك شيئا . يا عبادي لو أن أولكم وآخركم وإنسكم وجنكم اجتمعوا في صعيد واحد. فسألوني فأعطيت كل إنسان منه ما يسألني ، لم ينقص ذلك من ملكي شيئاً . إلا كما ينقص البحر أن يخمس فيه المخيط ، يا عبادي هذه أعمالكم أحفظها عليكم . فمن وجد خيرا فليحمد ، ومن وجد غير ذلك ، فلا يلومن إلا نفسه . . الله قالت المعتزلة : هذا الخبر يؤكد مذهبنا من وجوه : الأول : إنه تعالى قال : إني حرمت الظلم على نفسي ، وهذا يدل على أنه تعالى قادر على الظلم . إذ لو لم يقدر على الظلم ، لما قال : « إني حرمته على نفسي ، لأنه يجري مجرى ما إذا قال : إني حرمت على نفسي أن أجمع بين النقيضين ، ومعلوم أنه ركيك الثاني : إنه تعالى لما بين أنه حرم الظلم على نفسه ، أوجب على العباد أن لا يظلم بعضهم بعضاً . ولو كان تعالى هو الذي يخلق الظلم فيهم ، لكان ظالماً . وأيضاً : فكيف يقول لهم : لا تظالموا مع أنه تعالى هو الذي يخلق ذلك الظلم فيهم ؟ . والثالث : قوله : « إنكم تخطئون بالليل والنهار ، وأنا أغفر الذنوب ولا أبالي ، فلو كان حصول ذلك الخطأ بخلق الله وإيجاده ، كما أن الغفران منه ، لم يكن في هذا التفضيل والتميز فائدة. وأيضاً : فإذا خلق الخطأ غيره فهو تعالى إنما غفر للعبد بسبب فعل ما فعله العبد ، وتصريح النص يبطل ذلك الرابع : إنه تعالى قال في آخر هذا الحديث : «هذه أعمالكم أحفظها عليكم، وهذا تصريح بأن هذه الأعمال أعمالنا ، لا أعمال الله . ثم قال : من وجد خيرا فليحمد الله ، وهذا يدل على أنه تعالى خلق القدرة على الفعل ، وهدى العبد إليه ، ووضع الدلائل عليه وأرشد إليه ، ومنع عنه أضداده . ثم قال : ( ومن وجد غير ذلك ، فلا يلومن إلا نفسه وهذا تصريح بأن المعاصي ليست من الله البتة
Do not wrong one another. O My servants, you err by night and day, and I forgive all sins, and I do not care. So ask forgiveness of Me, I will forgive you. O My servants, all of you are hungry except those I have fed, so ask Me for food, I will feed you. O My servants, all of you are naked except those I have clothed, so ask Me for clothing, I will clothe you. O My servants, if the first of you and the last of you, humans and jinn, were upon the most pious heart of a single man, that would not increase anything in My kingdom. O My servants, if the first of you and the last of you, humans and jinn, gathered in one plain, and asked Me, and I gave every person among them what he asked, that would not diminish from My kingdom anything, except as the ocean is diminished when a needle is dipped into it. O My servants, these are your deeds which I preserve for you. So whoever finds good, let him praise Allah, and whoever finds other than that, let him blame no one but himself. The Mu'tazila said: This report confirms our school in several aspects: First: He, exalted, said: 'I have forbidden injustice to Myself'. This indicates that He, exalted, is capable of injustice. For if He were not capable of injustice, He would not have said 'I have forbidden it to Myself', because that would be like saying 'I have forbidden Myself to combine two opposites', and it is known that this is feeble. Second: When He, exalted, showed that He has forbidden injustice to Himself, He obligated the servants not to wrong one another. If He, exalted, were the one who creates injustice in them, then He would be unjust. Also: How can He say to them 'do not wrong one another' while He, exalted, is the one who creates that injustice in them? Third: His saying: 'You err by night and day, and I forgive sins and do not care'. If the occurrence of that error were by Allah's creation and bringing into existence, just as forgiveness is from Him, then there would be no benefit in this differentiation and distinction. Also: If He creates the error in others, then He, exalted, only forgives the servant due to the action which the servant has done, and the explicit text nullifies that. Fourth: He, exalted, said at the end of this hadith: 'These are your deeds which I preserve for you'. This is an explicit statement that these deeds are our deeds, not Allah's deeds. Then He said: 'Whoever finds good, let him praise Allah'. This indicates that He, exalted, created the ability for the action, guided the servant to it, placed the proofs upon it, directed him to it, and prevented its opposites from him. Then He said: 'And whoever finds other than that, let him blame no one but himself'. This is an explicit statement that sins are not from Allah at all.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage presents a hadith qudsi (sacred hadith) and then four arguments (wujuh) drawn from it by the Mu'tazila to support their doctrine of human free will and divine justice. The hadith reports God addressing His servants, emphasizing His self-forbiddance of injustice, His forgiveness, His provision, and that deeds belong to the servants. The Mu'tazila interpret it as proof that humans are the agents of their own actions, not God. The first argument: God's statement 'I have forbidden injustice to Myself' implies that He is capable of injustice (otherwise the forbidding is meaningless), but He chooses not to do it. This is contrasted with the impossibility of forbidding something inherently impossible (like combining opposites). The second argument: Since God commands people not to wrong each other, if God Himself created the injustice in them, He would be unjust and the command would be contradictory. The third argument: The distinction between God's forgiveness and human error shows that error is not created by God; if it were, there would be no special merit in forgiveness. The fourth argument: God says 'These are your deeds', explicitly attributing actions to humans, not to God. Also, the command to praise God for good and blame only oneself for evil shows that sins are entirely from the human self, not from God.

Key Terms

ظلم
قدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some interpret the hadith to deny human free will, arguing that everything is from God.
Correction: The hadith explicitly says 'these are your deeds' and 'blame no one but himself', supporting human agency.

Checkpoint
What does the hadith instruct a person who finds 'other than good' (i.e., evil) to do?
A) Blame God
B) Blame Satan
C) Blame no one but himself
D) Seek forgiveness

Key Takeaway
God's servants are responsible for their own deeds; good is from God's grace, evil from oneself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, when something goes wrong, do you instinctively blame circumstances, other people, or even God? After reading this hadith, where must your blame ultimately rest? Will you commit to saying 'I am responsible' the next time you make a mistake? If not, what holds you back?
?
The hadith says that even if all of humanity and jinn were the most pious, it would not increase God's kingdom. Does that make your worship feel pointless? Or does it free you to worship God purely for His sake, not to gain His advantage? Examine your heart: are you seeking to benefit God or to fulfill your duty? Answer honestly.
?
Imagine standing before God and He says to you, 'These are your deeds.' Will you be able to praise Him for the good, or will you have excuses for the evil? Right now, is there a sin you have been blaming on something else? What is it? Make a specific step today to own it and seek God's forgiveness.

First Argument: God Capable of Injustice
First Mu'tazilite argument from the hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first Mu'tazilite argument from the hadith, which infers God's ability to commit injustice from His statement 'I have forbidden it to Myself'.

Core Idea
Forbidding a thing implies ability to do it.

The Mu'tazila begin their case by focusing on God's declaration that He has forbidden injustice to Himself. They argue that this statement would be meaningless if God were inherently incapable of injustice, just as it would be absurd to say 'I forbid Myself from combining opposites'. This establishes that God has the power to do injustice but refrains by choice.

Guided Path
1
Read the first argument passage
Read the Arabic and translation of the first argument carefully. Note how the Mu'tazila connect God's statement to His capability.
2
Understand the logic
The argument is that forbidding something presupposes the possibility of doing it. If God were powerless to do injustice, the forbiddance would be meaningless.
Contrast with forbidding impossible acts like combining opposites.
3
Consider the implications
Why does this matter for free will? If God can do injustice but doesn't, then His justice is voluntary. Similarly, humans can choose evil or good.
This argument supports the Mu'tazilite view that actions are not compelled by God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلا تظالموا . يا عبادي إنكم الذين تخطئون بالليل والنهار وأنا أغفر الذنوب جميعاً ، ولا أبالي . فاستغفروني أغفر لكم . يا عبادي كلكم جائع إلا أطعمته فاستطعموني أطعمكم . يا عبادي كلكم عاري إلا من كسوته فاستكسوني أكسكم يا عبادي لو أن أولكم وآخركم وإنسكم وجنكم كانوا على أتقى قلب رجل واحد لم يزد ذلك شيئا . يا عبادي لو أن أولكم وآخركم وإنسكم وجنكم اجتمعوا في صعيد واحد. فسألوني فأعطيت كل إنسان منه ما يسألني ، لم ينقص ذلك من ملكي شيئاً . إلا كما ينقص البحر أن يخمس فيه المخيط ، يا عبادي هذه أعمالكم أحفظها عليكم . فمن وجد خيرا فليحمد ، ومن وجد غير ذلك ، فلا يلومن إلا نفسه . . الله قالت المعتزلة : هذا الخبر يؤكد مذهبنا من وجوه : الأول : إنه تعالى قال : إني حرمت الظلم على نفسي ، وهذا يدل على أنه تعالى قادر على الظلم . إذ لو لم يقدر على الظلم ، لما قال : « إني حرمته على نفسي ، لأنه يجري مجرى ما إذا قال : إني حرمت على نفسي أن أجمع بين النقيضين ، ومعلوم أنه ركيك الثاني : إنه تعالى لما بين أنه حرم الظلم على نفسه ، أوجب على العباد أن لا يظلم بعضهم بعضاً . ولو كان تعالى هو الذي يخلق الظلم فيهم ، لكان ظالماً . وأيضاً : فكيف يقول لهم : لا تظالموا مع أنه تعالى هو الذي يخلق ذلك الظلم فيهم ؟ . والثالث : قوله : « إنكم تخطئون بالليل والنهار ، وأنا أغفر الذنوب ولا أبالي ، فلو كان حصول ذلك الخطأ بخلق الله وإيجاده ، كما أن الغفران منه ، لم يكن في هذا التفضيل والتميز فائدة. وأيضاً : فإذا خلق الخطأ غيره فهو تعالى إنما غفر للعبد بسبب فعل ما فعله العبد ، وتصريح النص يبطل ذلك الرابع : إنه تعالى قال في آخر هذا الحديث : «هذه أعمالكم أحفظها عليكم، وهذا تصريح بأن هذه الأعمال أعمالنا ، لا أعمال الله . ثم قال : من وجد خيرا فليحمد الله ، وهذا يدل على أنه تعالى خلق القدرة على الفعل ، وهدى العبد إليه ، ووضع الدلائل عليه وأرشد إليه ، ومنع عنه أضداده . ثم قال : ( ومن وجد غير ذلك ، فلا يلومن إلا نفسه وهذا تصريح بأن المعاصي ليست من الله البتة
Do not wrong one another. O My servants, you err by night and day, and I forgive all sins, and I do not care. So ask forgiveness of Me, I will forgive you. O My servants, all of you are hungry except those I have fed, so ask Me for food, I will feed you. O My servants, all of you are naked except those I have clothed, so ask Me for clothing, I will clothe you. O My servants, if the first of you and the last of you, humans and jinn, were upon the most pious heart of a single man, that would not increase anything in My kingdom. O My servants, if the first of you and the last of you, humans and jinn, gathered in one plain, and asked Me, and I gave every person among them what he asked, that would not diminish from My kingdom anything, except as the ocean is diminished when a needle is dipped into it. O My servants, these are your deeds which I preserve for you. So whoever finds good, let him praise Allah, and whoever finds other than that, let him blame no one but himself. The Mu'tazila said: This report confirms our school in several aspects: First: He, exalted, said: 'I have forbidden injustice to Myself'. This indicates that He, exalted, is capable of injustice. For if He were not capable of injustice, He would not have said 'I have forbidden it to Myself', because that would be like saying 'I have forbidden Myself to combine two opposites', and it is known that this is feeble. Second: When He, exalted, showed that He has forbidden injustice to Himself, He obligated the servants not to wrong one another. If He, exalted, were the one who creates injustice in them, then He would be unjust. Also: How can He say to them 'do not wrong one another' while He, exalted, is the one who creates that injustice in them? Third: His saying: 'You err by night and day, and I forgive sins and do not care'. If the occurrence of that error were by Allah's creation and bringing into existence, just as forgiveness is from Him, then there would be no benefit in this differentiation and distinction. Also: If He creates the error in others, then He, exalted, only forgives the servant due to the action which the servant has done, and the explicit text nullifies that. Fourth: He, exalted, said at the end of this hadith: 'These are your deeds which I preserve for you'. This is an explicit statement that these deeds are our deeds, not Allah's deeds. Then He said: 'Whoever finds good, let him praise Allah'. This indicates that He, exalted, created the ability for the action, guided the servant to it, placed the proofs upon it, directed him to it, and prevented its opposites from him. Then He said: 'And whoever finds other than that, let him blame no one but himself'. This is an explicit statement that sins are not from Allah at all.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage presents a hadith qudsi (sacred hadith) and then four arguments (wujuh) drawn from it by the Mu'tazila to support their doctrine of human free will and divine justice. The hadith reports God addressing His servants, emphasizing His self-forbiddance of injustice, His forgiveness, His provision, and that deeds belong to the servants. The Mu'tazila interpret it as proof that humans are the agents of their own actions, not God. The first argument: God's statement 'I have forbidden injustice to Myself' implies that He is capable of injustice (otherwise the forbidding is meaningless), but He chooses not to do it. This is contrasted with the impossibility of forbidding something inherently impossible (like combining opposites). The second argument: Since God commands people not to wrong each other, if God Himself created the injustice in them, He would be unjust and the command would be contradictory. The third argument: The distinction between God's forgiveness and human error shows that error is not created by God; if it were, there would be no special merit in forgiveness. The fourth argument: God says 'These are your deeds', explicitly attributing actions to humans, not to God. Also, the command to praise God for good and blame only oneself for evil shows that sins are entirely from the human self, not from God.

Key Terms
ظلم
قدرة
حرّم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God cannot commit injustice under any circumstances.
Correction: Mu'tazila argue He can, but forbids it to Himself, showing His justice is voluntary.

Checkpoint
According to the first argument, what would be the consequence if God were not capable of injustice?
A) The hadith would be false
B) His statement of forbiddance would be feeble
C) He would be unjust
D) Humans would have no free will

Key Takeaway
God's self-forbiddance of injustice implies He is capable of it, otherwise the forbiddance would be empty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have the ability to harm others with your words or actions. When you refrain, is it because you cannot, or because you choose not to? How does God's example of forbidding injustice to Himself while being capable of it challenge your excuses for wrongdoing?
?
If God, with all power, restrains Himself from injustice, what does that say about your own use of power when you are in a position of authority over someone? When have you justified a small injustice because you could?
?
The Mu'tazila say God's forbiddance of injustice proves He could do it but doesn't. Does your own 'self-forbiddance' of sin come from a real choice or from lack of opportunity? What would change if you truly believed you could do it but choose not to?

Second Argument: Command against Injustice
Second Mu'tazilite argument from the hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second Mu'tazilite argument, which holds that God's command not to wrong one another would be contradictory if God Himself created injustice.

Core Idea
God commanding justice contradicts Him creating injustice.

The Mu'tazila argue that since God commands people not to wrong each other, it would be inconsistent for Him to be the creator of that very injustice. If He created the injustice in them, then He would be the unjust one, and His command would be absurd. This argument underscores that humans must be the agents of their own wrongful acts.

Guided Path
1
Read the second argument
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the two parts: God's command and the implication if He created injustice.
2
Understand the contradiction
If God creates the injustice, then He is the unjust one, and commanding against it would be like commanding against His own action.
This would make the command hypocritical.
3
Connect to free will
The only way to avoid contradiction is that humans themselves produce their own unjust acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Third Argument: Distinction Between Error and Forgiveness
Third Mu'tazilite argument from the hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third Mu'tazilite argument, which uses the distinction between human error and divine forgiveness to argue that errors are not created by God.

Core Idea
If God created both error and forgiveness, there would be no distinction.

The Mu'tazila draw attention to God's statement that He forgives sins. They argue that if God Himself created the errors that people commit, then there would be no meaningful difference between God causing the sin and God forgiving it. The very fact that forgiveness has value shows that the sin is not caused by God, but by the human.

Guided Path
1
Read the third argument
Read the Arabic and translation. Focus on the logic that if God created both error and forgiveness, then forgiveness would have no special merit.
2
Analyze the distinction
The argument says: if errors were from God, then forgiveness would be like forgiving oneself, which is pointless.
Contrast with the hadith's clear separation of error (by humans) and forgiveness (from God).
3
Implication for free will
This shows that errors must originate from human choice, not divine creation.

فلا تظالموا . يا عبادي إنكم الذين تخطئون بالليل والنهار وأنا أغفر الذنوب جميعاً ، ولا أبالي . فاستغفروني أغفر لكم . يا عبادي كلكم جائع إلا أطعمته فاستطعموني أطعمكم . يا عبادي كلكم عاري إلا من كسوته فاستكسوني أكسكم يا عبادي لو أن أولكم وآخركم وإنسكم وجنكم كانوا على أتقى قلب رجل واحد لم يزد ذلك شيئا . يا عبادي لو أن أولكم وآخركم وإنسكم وجنكم اجتمعوا في صعيد واحد. فسألوني فأعطيت كل إنسان منه ما يسألني ، لم ينقص ذلك من ملكي شيئاً . إلا كما ينقص البحر أن يخمس فيه المخيط ، يا عبادي هذه أعمالكم أحفظها عليكم . فمن وجد خيرا فليحمد ، ومن وجد غير ذلك ، فلا يلومن إلا نفسه . . الله قالت المعتزلة : هذا الخبر يؤكد مذهبنا من وجوه : الأول : إنه تعالى قال : إني حرمت الظلم على نفسي ، وهذا يدل على أنه تعالى قادر على الظلم . إذ لو لم يقدر على الظلم ، لما قال : « إني حرمته على نفسي ، لأنه يجري مجرى ما إذا قال : إني حرمت على نفسي أن أجمع بين النقيضين ، ومعلوم أنه ركيك الثاني : إنه تعالى لما بين أنه حرم الظلم على نفسه ، أوجب على العباد أن لا يظلم بعضهم بعضاً . ولو كان تعالى هو الذي يخلق الظلم فيهم ، لكان ظالماً . وأيضاً : فكيف يقول لهم : لا تظالموا مع أنه تعالى هو الذي يخلق ذلك الظلم فيهم ؟ . والثالث : قوله : « إنكم تخطئون بالليل والنهار ، وأنا أغفر الذنوب ولا أبالي ، فلو كان حصول ذلك الخطأ بخلق الله وإيجاده ، كما أن الغفران منه ، لم يكن في هذا التفضيل والتميز فائدة. وأيضاً : فإذا خلق الخطأ غيره فهو تعالى إنما غفر للعبد بسبب فعل ما فعله العبد ، وتصريح النص يبطل ذلك الرابع : إنه تعالى قال في آخر هذا الحديث : «هذه أعمالكم أحفظها عليكم، وهذا تصريح بأن هذه الأعمال أعمالنا ، لا أعمال الله . ثم قال : من وجد خيرا فليحمد الله ، وهذا يدل على أنه تعالى خلق القدرة على الفعل ، وهدى العبد إليه ، ووضع الدلائل عليه وأرشد إليه ، ومنع عنه أضداده . ثم قال : ( ومن وجد غير ذلك ، فلا يلومن إلا نفسه وهذا تصريح بأن المعاصي ليست من الله البتة
Do not wrong one another. O My servants, you err by night and day, and I forgive all sins, and I do not care. So ask forgiveness of Me, I will forgive you. O My servants, all of you are hungry except those I have fed, so ask Me for food, I will feed you. O My servants, all of you are naked except those I have clothed, so ask Me for clothing, I will clothe you. O My servants, if the first of you and the last of you, humans and jinn, were upon the most pious heart of a single man, that would not increase anything in My kingdom. O My servants, if the first of you and the last of you, humans and jinn, gathered in one plain, and asked Me, and I gave every person among them what he asked, that would not diminish from My kingdom anything, except as the ocean is diminished when a needle is dipped into it. O My servants, these are your deeds which I preserve for you. So whoever finds good, let him praise Allah, and whoever finds other than that, let him blame no one but himself. The Mu'tazila said: This report confirms our school in several aspects: First: He, exalted, said: 'I have forbidden injustice to Myself'. This indicates that He, exalted, is capable of injustice. For if He were not capable of injustice, He would not have said 'I have forbidden it to Myself', because that would be like saying 'I have forbidden Myself to combine two opposites', and it is known that this is feeble. Second: When He, exalted, showed that He has forbidden injustice to Himself, He obligated the servants not to wrong one another. If He, exalted, were the one who creates injustice in them, then He would be unjust. Also: How can He say to them 'do not wrong one another' while He, exalted, is the one who creates that injustice in them? Third: His saying: 'You err by night and day, and I forgive sins and do not care'. If the occurrence of that error were by Allah's creation and bringing into existence, just as forgiveness is from Him, then there would be no benefit in this differentiation and distinction. Also: If He creates the error in others, then He, exalted, only forgives the servant due to the action which the servant has done, and the explicit text nullifies that. Fourth: He, exalted, said at the end of this hadith: 'These are your deeds which I preserve for you'. This is an explicit statement that these deeds are our deeds, not Allah's deeds. Then He said: 'Whoever finds good, let him praise Allah'. This indicates that He, exalted, created the ability for the action, guided the servant to it, placed the proofs upon it, directed him to it, and prevented its opposites from him. Then He said: 'And whoever finds other than that, let him blame no one but himself'. This is an explicit statement that sins are not from Allah at all.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage presents a hadith qudsi (sacred hadith) and then four arguments (wujuh) drawn from it by the Mu'tazila to support their doctrine of human free will and divine justice. The hadith reports God addressing His servants, emphasizing His self-forbiddance of injustice, His forgiveness, His provision, and that deeds belong to the servants. The Mu'tazila interpret it as proof that humans are the agents of their own actions, not God. The first argument: God's statement 'I have forbidden injustice to Myself' implies that He is capable of injustice (otherwise the forbidding is meaningless), but He chooses not to do it. This is contrasted with the impossibility of forbidding something inherently impossible (like combining opposites). The second argument: Since God commands people not to wrong each other, if God Himself created the injustice in them, He would be unjust and the command would be contradictory. The third argument: The distinction between God's forgiveness and human error shows that error is not created by God; if it were, there would be no special merit in forgiveness. The fourth argument: God says 'These are your deeds', explicitly attributing actions to humans, not to God. Also, the command to praise God for good and blame only oneself for evil shows that sins are entirely from the human self, not from God.

Key Terms
خطأ
مغفرة
خلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's forgiveness is purely arbitrary and unrelated to human action.
Correction: The Mu'tazila argue forgiveness is a response to human sin, which must be freely chosen.

Checkpoint
What would be the consequence if both error and forgiveness were created by God?
A) Forgiveness would be more meaningful
B) There would be no benefit in distinguishing them
C) Humans would be innocent
D) God would be unjust

Key Takeaway
The distinction between human error and divine forgiveness shows that errors are not created by God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you take full ownership of it, or do you find yourself subtly attributing it to Allah’s decree? How does this hadith’s emphasis on 'you err' challenge your tendency to shift responsibility?
?
If you truly believed that your mistakes are entirely your own doing, would you still seek Allah’s forgiveness with the same urgency? How does your understanding of human agency affect the sincerity of your repentance?
?
The hadith says Allah forgives 'and does not care.' Does the magnitude of Allah’s forgiveness ever make you minimize the seriousness of your errors? How does the Mu'tazilite argument—that error is your own—force you to confront the weight of each sin?

Fourth Argument: Deeds Are Ours
Fourth Mu'tazilite argument from the hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth Mu'tazilite argument, which takes God's statement 'These are your deeds' as explicit proof that actions belong to humans, not to God.

Core Idea
God says deeds are ours, so we create them.

The Mu'tazila point to the direct language of the hadith: 'These are your deeds which I preserve for you'. They argue that this is an explicit attribution of actions to humans. Then, the instruction to praise God for good and blame oneself for evil further reinforces that good comes from God's guidance and evil from one's own self. This final argument clinches the case for human free will.

Guided Path
1
Read the fourth argument
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the direct quote 'These are your deeds' and the subsequent commands.
2
Analyze the attribution
The words 'your deeds' clearly ascribe actions to humans. The Mu'tazila stress that this is explicit, not metaphorical.
3
Understand the praise and blame
Praising God for good shows He provided guidance and ability. Blaming oneself for evil shows the evil originates from oneself.
This distinguishes between God's role (creating capability, guidance) and human role (choosing to use it rightly or wrongly).

Source Text
