The Meaning of Divine Leading Astray (iḍlāl)
The author explains iḍlāl as causing preponderance of misguidance, with possible counteraction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nuanced meaning of iḍlāl in kalam, as a causal factor that can be counteracted.

Core Idea
God's leading astray is a causal factor, not an irresistible force.

In theological discussions about divine action and human responsibility, the term iḍlāl often raises questions. If God leads someone astray, does that force them into misguidance? This passage from al-Maṭālib al-ʿĀliyah clarifies that iḍlāl means doing what necessitates a preponderance of misguidance, but that such necessitation can be opposed by another factor.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation to get the literal meaning. Notice the structure: an objection is implied, then answered.
The phrase 'قلنا' indicates the author's response.
2
Understand the objection
The passage begins by referencing an objection: if God led him astray, how can he not be astray? This is a common challenge against divine justice.
3
Grasp the definition
The author defines iḍlāl as 'doing that which necessitates preponderance of the side of misguidance' (فعل ما يقتضي ترجيح جانب الضلال). Note the key term 'يقتضي' (necessitates) — it indicates a causal tendency, not absolute determination.
4
See the nuance: counteraction
The author explains that the necessitating factor (المقتضى) may be opposed by something else (معارضاً بشيء آخر), in which case it ceases to be necessitating. This shows that divine iḍlāl does not always result in actual misguidance.
This nuance preserves both divine action and human accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( إنه تعالى أضله فما أضل ) قلنا : المفهوم من الإضلال فعل ما يقتضي ترجيح جانب الضلال . ثم إن المقتضى قد يصير معارضاً بشيء آخر ، فيخرج عن كونه مقتضيا . وقد لا يصير كذلك
His statement: 'Indeed, He led him astray, so he was not led astray?' We say: The understood meaning of iḍlāl is doing that which necessitates preponderance of the side of misguidance. Then, the necessitating factor may be opposed by something else, thus it ceases to be necessitating, or it may not be so.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection that if God leads someone astray, that person cannot fail to be astray. The author clarifies that iḍlāl means doing something that necessitates (yaqtaḍī) the preponderance of misguidance. However, this necessitating factor (muqtaḍā) may sometimes be opposed by another factor, in which case it ceases to be effective, or it may not be opposed, and then the person is indeed led astray. This explains why a person might not be misled despite God's iḍlāl.

Key Terms
الإضلال
المقتضى
ترجيح جانب الضلال
المعارضة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God's iḍlāl is always effective and irresistible, so that if God leads someone astray, that person cannot possibly avoid being astray.
Correction: The author explains that iḍlāl is a necessitating factor, but it can be opposed by something else, in which case it ceases to necessitate. Thus, divine leading astray does not always result in actual misguidance; it is a causal tendency that can be counteracted.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does iḍlāl mean in this context?
A) Directly creating disbelief
B) Doing that which necessitates preponderance of misguidance
C) Preventing guidance
D) Withholding grace

Key Takeaway
iḍlāl is a necessitating factor for misguidance that can be counteracted, so divine leading astray does not always result in actual misguidance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself repeatedly drawn to a sin, do you recognize that God's iḍlāl (as a causal inclination) may be at play, but also that you have the capacity to oppose it? What concrete step will you take today to counteract that inclination?
?
If God's leading astray can be counteracted, then your misguidance is not inevitable. Does that thought make you more responsible for your actions? How will you respond to that responsibility starting now?
?
What if the opposing factor that counteracts iḍlāl is your own sincere supplication? Will you commit to praying to God to remove the inclination towards misguidance from your heart? Write down one dua you will make tonight.

Guidance is Allah's Direct Creation
Refutation of an objection about creating misguidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God's sending of messengers does not obligate Him to guide everyone; rather, guidance is a direct creation of Allah, and the literal meaning of iḍlāl is creating misguidance.

Core Idea
Guidance is not automatic from proofs; it is Allah's direct creation.

The final objection raised against the Ash‘arite position is a seeming contradiction: if God sends messengers with clear language to explain, why would He then create misguidance? The author shows that completing the proof does not guarantee guidance; guidance itself is a separate creation of Allah. This lesson unpacks this response and its Quranic support.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to get the overall argument.
Pay attention to the objection quoted at the beginning.
2
Identify the objection and response
Find the opponent's objection and the author's response. Notice how the author distinguishes between completing the explanation (itmām al-bayān) and creating guidance (khalq al-hidāyah).
3
Analyze the Quranic support
Read the verse quoted (Quran 6:111) and see how it reinforces the point that even extraordinary signs do not force belief without Allah's will.
4
Understand the conclusion on literal meaning
The author concludes that the literal meaning of iḍlāl is creating misguidance, and all allegorical interpretations are invalid. Reflect on why this is important for the overall argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وكيف يليق أن يقول : ( وما أرسلنا من رسول إلا بلسان )... ثم يقول عقيبه : إني أخلق الجهل في البعض ، والعلم في البعض )؟ قلنا : إنه تعالى بين أنه بعث الرسول إليهم بلسانهم ، حتى يكمل البيان ، ويظهر الدليل، ولكنه يضل البعض ويهدي البعض ، ومع ذلك لا يظهر أنه لا يكفي في حصول الهداية تكميل البيان ، وإيضاح الحجة والبرهان . بل الدلائل وإن ظهرت ، والبراهين وإن بهرت ، إلا أنه ما لم يخلق الله الهداية ، لم يحصل المقصود . وهذا الكلام من هذا الوجه في غاية الانتظام . ونظيره قوله تعالى : ( ولو أننا نزلنا إليهم الملائكة ، وكلمهم الموت ، وحشرنا عليهم كل شيء قبلاً ، ما كانوا ليؤمنوا إلا أن يشاء الله ) فثبت : أن الدلائل التي ذكروها في بيان أنه لا يمكن حمل لفظ الإضلال على خلق الإضلال ، كلها واهية ساقطة . وإذا كانت حقيقة لفظ الإضلال هو خلق الضلال ، وثبت : أن الأصل في الكلام هو الحقيقة ، وجب حمل اللفظ عليه ، والإعراض عما ذكروه من التأويلات ، وحل اللفظ على المجازات . والله أعلم
His statement: 'How is it fitting that He says: “And We sent not a messenger except with the language [of his people]”… then He says after it: “I create ignorance in some and knowledge in some”?' We say: Indeed, God Most High clarified that He sent the messenger to them in their language so that the explanation would be complete and the proof would appear, but He leads some astray and guides some. Yet it does not appear that completing the explanation and clarifying the argument and proof is sufficient for achieving guidance. Rather, even if the proofs appear and the evidences are dazzling, unless God creates guidance, the intended result is not achieved. This speech from this perspective is extremely well-ordered. Its parallel is His statement: 'Even if We had sent down to them the angels, and the dead spoke to them, and We gathered before them every thing, they would not believe unless God willed.' Thus it is established that the proofs they mentioned to show that the word iḍlāl cannot mean creating iḍlāl are all weak and invalid. And since the true meaning of the word iḍlāl is creating misguidance, and it is established that the default in speech is the literal meaning, it is necessary to interpret the word accordingly, and to disregard the allegorical interpretations they mentioned and to discard metaphorical meanings. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This is the final and longest objection-answer, concluding the discussion. The opponent questions how God can say He sent messengers with their language to clarify, and then say He creates ignorance in some and knowledge in some—seeming contradiction. The author responds that God sent messengers to complete the explanation (itmām al-bayān) and make the proof clear (iẓhār al-dalīl), but that does not guarantee guidance. Guidance only occurs when God creates it (khalq al-hidāyah). The author then cites Quran 6:111 to support the idea that even if all signs come, people will not believe unless God wills. He concludes that all objections based on incoherence are weak, and the literal meaning of iḍlāl as creating misguidance must be upheld, rejecting allegorical interpretations.

Key Terms
الإضلال
خلق الضلال
تكميل البيان
خلق الهداية
الحقيقة
المجاز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That if God sends clear proofs, then He is obliged to guide everyone.
Correction: The author shows that completing the explanation does not necessitate guidance; guidance is a direct creation of Allah, and He may will misguidance for some.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is necessary for the intended result of guidance to be achieved?
A) The completion of the messenger's explanation
B) The appearance of clear proofs
C) God's creation of guidance
D) The person's free will

Key Takeaway
The literal meaning of iḍlāl is creating misguidance, and guidance is a direct creation of Allah, not merely a result of proofs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that because you have clearly heard the truth, you are automatically guided? Where in your heart can you point to a place where Allah has directly created guidance, not just information? What will you do today to beg Him for that creation?
?
The author says proofs can be dazzling but still insufficient. Recall a moment when a powerful proof left you unchanged. Why do you think your heart remained unmoved? Are you willing to admit that only Allah can turn knowledge into faith, and will you ask Him to do that for you right now?
?
If guidance is a direct creation of Allah and not a natural result of evidence, then how much of your spiritual effort is spent on arguments versus on supplication? Is your trust really in the Creator of guidance or in the cleverness of your own reasoning? Commit to one concrete change in your du'a today.

Defending the Literal Meaning of Idhal
Razi defends the literal meaning of idhal as creation of misguidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi defends the literal interpretation of 'idhal' as God's creation of misguidance, and why clear proofs alone are insufficient for guidance.

Core Idea
Clear evidence does not automatically produce guidance; God must create it.

Razi addresses a critical objection: if God sends messengers with clear evidence, why does He still create ignorance and knowledge? In this passage, he argues that completing the proof does not suffice for guidance; God's direct creation of guidance is required. This establishes the literal meaning of 'idhal' as creation of misguidance.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the initial objection and the response beginning with 'قلنا'. Identify the key claim: that God sends messengers with clear language but still misguides some.
The objection is implicit; the response directly addresses it.
2
Examine the Quranic support
Razi cites Quran 6:111 to show that even if angels came and the dead spoke, people would not believe unless God willed. This reinforces that guidance depends on God's creation, not just evidence.
3
Understand the conclusion
Since the literal meaning of 'idhal' is creation of misguidance, and the rule in speech is to use literal meaning, any figurative interpretation must be rejected. This is the core conclusion.
The passage ends with 'والله أعلم'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأجل أن يكون البيان كافياً تاماً . ثم يقول عقيبه : إني أخلق الجهل في البعض ، والعلم في البعض ) ؟ قلنا : إنه تعالى بين أنه بعث الرسول إليهم بلسانهم ، حتى يكمل البيان ، ويظهر الدليل، ولكنه يضل البعض ويهدي البعض ، ومع ذلك لا يظهر أنه لا يكفي في حصول الهداية تكميل البيان ، وإيضاح الحجة والبرهان . بل الدلائل وإن ظهرت ، والبراهين وإن بهرت ، إلا أنه ما لم يخلق الله الهداية ، لم يحصل المقصود . وهذا الكلام من هذا الوجه في غاية الانتظام . ونظيره قوله تعالى : ( ولو أننا نزلنا إليهم الملائكة ، وكلمهم الموت ، وحشرنا عليهم كل شيء قبلاً ، ما كانوا ليؤمنوا إلا أن يشاء الله (٢) فثبت : أن الدلائل التي ذكروها في بيان أنه لا يمكن حمل لفظ الإضلال على خلق الإضلال ، كلها واهية ساقطة . وإذا كانت حقيقة لفظ الإضلال هو خلق الضلال ، وثبت : أن الأصل في الكلام هو الحقيقة ، وجب حمل اللفظ عليه ، والإعراض عما ذكروه من التأويلات ، وحل اللفظ على المجازات (٣). والله أعلم
In order that the explanation be complete and perfect. Then he says after it: 'I create ignorance in some and knowledge in some'? We said: He, exalted, made clear that He sent the messenger to them in their own language, so that the explanation is complete and the proof appears, but He misguides some and guides some, and despite that, it does not appear that completing the explanation and clarifying the argument and proof suffices for obtaining guidance. Rather, even if the proofs appear and the evidences dazzle, unless God creates guidance, the objective is not achieved. And this speech, from this aspect, is extremely well ordered. And its parallel is His statement, exalted: (And even if We sent down to them the angels, and the dead spoke to them, and We gathered before them every thing face to face, they would not believe unless God willed) (2). So it is established: that the proofs they mentioned in showing that it is not possible to interpret the word 'idhal' as creation of misguidance are all weak and invalid. And since the reality of the word 'idhal' is the creation of misguidance, and it is established that the principle in speech is literal meaning, it is obligatory to apply the word to it, and to turn away from the interpretations they mentioned, and to understand the word figuratively (3). And God knows best.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer argument. It begins by quoting an objection: someone claims that God says 'I create ignorance in some and knowledge in some,' implying that the clear communication of the message is sufficient for guidance. The response (قلنا) explains that God indeed sent messengers with clear language, but He still misguides some and guides others. The completion of the proof alone does not guarantee guidance; God's creation of guidance (الهداية) is necessary. This is supported by Quran 6:111, which states that even if angels came and the dead spoke, people would not believe unless God wills. From this, the author concludes that the proofs offered by opponents to deny that 'idhal' means 'creation of misguidance' are weak. Since the literal meaning of 'idhal' is creation of misguidance, and the rule is to take words literally, the only correct interpretation is the literal one, rejecting their metaphorical interpretations. The passage ends with 'والله أعلم' (God knows best).

الهداية (hidaya)
الضلال (dalal)
البيان (bayan)
الدليل (dalil)
التأويل (ta'wil)
المجاز (majaz)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume that if clear evidence is presented, guidance automatically follows.
Correction: This passage shows that even with the clearest proofs, guidance depends on God's creation of faith.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the true meaning of the word 'idhal' (إضلال)?
A) To call someone astray
B) To create misguidance in someone
C) To provide misleading evidence
D) To abandon someone without guidance

Key Takeaway
The literal meaning of 'idhal' is God's creation of misguidance, and clear evidence does not suffice for guidance without God's creation of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever relied on your own intelligence or the clarity of an argument to bring you closer to God, only to find yourself still distant? Does this lesson force you to acknowledge that even the clearest proofs are powerless without God's creation of guidance in your heart? Will you today plead to Him for that guidance as a helpless beggar, not as a scholar who has figured it out?
?
When you see someone who rejects Islam despite the clear evidence, do you become frustrated or judgmental? This lesson says that guidance is entirely in God's hands. How does that change your attitude toward them? Will you now turn your frustration into dua for them, recognizing that only God can create faith?
?
If the literal meaning of idhal is that God creates misguidance, does that make you question His justice? Or does it humble you to realize that you are not entitled to guidance, but it is a pure gift? Will you thank Him tonight for the gift of faith, knowing you did not earn it?
